Acknowledgment of Bequest After Division: The Hanafi Rule of Self-Binding and the Istihsan-Qiyas Dispute
Multi-part ruling on acknowledgment of will after division with comparisons to wadi'a and debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that an heir's acknowledgment binds only his own share, calculate the legatee's entitlement in multi-heir scenarios, and explain why the majority (istihsan) overrides Zufr's qiyas.

Core Idea
An heir's acknowledgment binds only his own share, so the legatee takes one-third of that share, not half.

When an heir acknowledges a bequest after the estate has been divided, the central principle is that his admission does not affect co-heirs. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling and the internal debate with Imam Zufr, who argued for a different proportion based on qiyas. You will work through multiple scenarios—consecutive and simultaneous acknowledgments, and comparisons with deposits and debts—to master this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acknowledgment scenario
Determine whether the acknowledgment is consecutive (separate) or simultaneous (connected). If consecutive, the first acknowledgment takes full priority. If simultaneous, the third is divided equally between the two legatees.
This distinction is analogous to acknowledgment of a deposit.
2
Isolate the acknowledging heir's share
After division, each heir has a separate share of the estate. The acknowledging heir's share is the only portion affected by his admission.
The co-heir's share remains untouched if he denies.
3
Apply the principle of self-binding (iqrar yasarr)
Hanafi law holds that an acknowledgment is valid only against the one who makes it. Therefore, the legatee's claim is limited to the acknowledging heir's share.
This is the basis for istihsan in this case.
4
Calculate the legatee's entitlement under istihsan
The legatee is entitled to one-third of the acknowledging heir's share (if the will was for one-third of the estate). This is the mufta bihi position.
For example, if each heir has 1000, the legatee gets 333.33 from the acknowledging heir.
5
Compare with Zufr's qiyas
Imam Zufr argued by qiyas that acknowledgment implies equality, so the legatee should take half of the acknowledging heir's share. Identify why the Hanafi majority rejects this: the legatee would then exceed one-third of the total estate if combined with the denying heir's share, violating the bequest limit.
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Zufr's view, the legatee gets 500 instead of 333.33.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا الذي ذكرنا كله إذا كان الإقرار للثاني منفصلاً عن الأول، فأما إذا كان متصلاً كان الثلث بينهما نصفين ونظير هذا الإقرار بالوديعة لو أقر أن هذا العبد عنده وديعة لفلان وفلان أو قال وديعة عنده ولفلان آخر متصلاً كان العبد بينهما نصفين كأنه قال هذا العبد وديعة عندي لفلان ثم قال لا بل لفلان فإن العبد كله للأول فكذا هذا قال: وإذا أقر الوارث بوصية درهم بعينها ثم أقر ذلك بعد بالثلث لآخر ثم رفع ذلك إلى القاضي فإنه يدفع إلى الأول وكان الجواب فيه كالجواب فيما إذا أقر بالثلث لآخر ثم رفع ذلك إلى القاضي فإنه يدفع الألف إلى الأول، ثم أقر بعد ذلك للثاني، فإن الثلث كله يدفع للأول ولا يكون للثاني فيه شيء كذلك هذا الجواب فيما لو أقر بوصية بغير عينها والجواب فيما لو أقر بألف بعينها لأن الوصايا تنفذ من الثلث فصار الثلث كله مستحقاً للأول بالإقرار الأول، وكان الجواب فيما لو أقر بألف قال محمد في الجامع في الرجل يموت ويترك وارثين وألفي درهم فيأخذ كل واحد منهما ألفاً فغاب أحدهما وأقر الحاضر لرجل أن الميت أوصى له بثلث أخذ المقر له من الحاضر ثلث ما في يده؛ فرق بين هذا ما وبين إذا أقر الحاضر بدين له فإنه يأخذ كل ذلك من نصيبه وإن أقر أحدهما بوديعة بعينها وذلك في نصيبه وكذبه الآخر فإنه يؤخذ ذلك كله من المقر، وإن أقر بوديعة مجهولة يستوفي الكل من نصيبه. ولو أقرأ أحدهما بشركة بينه وبين الآخر وكذبه الآخر صح في نصيبه ويقسم ما في يده بين المقر والمقر له ولا يأخذ المقر له من الجاحد شيئاً لأن إقرار كل مقر يصح في حقه ولا يصح في حق غيره ونظير هذا ما قالوا في رجل مات وترك بنتين وأقرت إحدى البنتين بأخ مجهول وكذبتها البنت الأخرى فإن الأخ المقر له يأخذ من نصيب البنت المقرة وفي الكافي : ابنان اقتسما تركه الأب ألفاً ثم أقر أحدهما الرجل أن الأب أوصى له بثلث ماله فالمقر يعطيه ثلث ما في يده استحساناً. وقال زفر يعطيه نصف ما في يده قياساً، ولو كان البنون ثلاثة والتركة ثلاثة آلاف فاقتسموها فجاء رجل وادعى أن الميت أوصى له بثلث ماله وصدقه واحد منهم فإنه يعطيه عند زفر ثلاثاً اخماس ما في يده، وعندنا يعطيه ثلث ما في يده.
And all of this that we mentioned is when the acknowledgment for the second is separate from the first. As for when it is connected, the third is between them in halves. An analogy for this is acknowledgment of a deposit: if he acknowledges that this slave is a deposit with him for so-and-so and so-and-so, or says 'a deposit with him and for another so-and-so' connectedly, the slave is between them in halves. It is as if he said 'this slave is a deposit with me for so-and-so' then said 'no, rather for so-and-so', then the entire slave is for the first. So is this. He said: If an heir acknowledges a bequest of a specific dirham, then afterwards acknowledges the third for another, then the matter is raised to the judge, he gives to the first. The answer in it is like the answer when he acknowledges the third for another, then raises it to the judge, then the one thousand is given to the first. Then he acknowledges afterwards for the second, then the entire third is given to the first and there is nothing for the second. Similarly, this answer is regarding what if he acknowledges a bequest without specification, and the answer regarding what if he acknowledges a specific one thousand, because bequests are executed from the third, so the entire third becomes entitled to the first by the first acknowledgment. And the answer regarding what if he acknowledges a thousand: Muhammad said in al-Jami': regarding a man who dies leaving two heirs and two thousand dirhams, so each takes one thousand, then one of them goes away, and the present heir acknowledges to a man that the deceased bequeathed to him a third, then the acknowledged person takes from the present heir a third of what is in his hand. The difference between this and when the present heir acknowledges a debt for him is that he takes all of that from his share. And if one of them acknowledges a specific deposit, and that is in his share, and the other denies him, then all of that is taken from the acknowledging one. And if he acknowledges an unspecified deposit, he collects all from his share. And if one of them acknowledges a partnership between him and the other, and the other denies him, it is valid in his share, and what is in his hand is divided between the acknowledging one and the acknowledged one, and the acknowledged one does not take anything from the denier, because the acknowledgment of each acknowledger is valid in his own right and not valid in the right of others. An analogy for this is what they said about a man who dies leaving two daughters, and one of the daughters acknowledges an unknown brother, and the other daughter denies her, then the acknowledged brother takes from the share of the acknowledging daughter. And in al-Kafi: Two sons divided their father's estate of one thousand, then one of them acknowledges to a man that the father bequeathed to him a third of his wealth. Then the acknowledger gives him a third of what is in his hand by istihsan. Zufr said: he gives him half of what is in his hand by qiyas. And if there were three sons and the estate was three thousand, so they divided it, then a man came and claimed that the deceased bequeathed to him a third of his wealth, and one of them confirmed him, then according to Zufr he gives him three-fifths of what is in his hand, and according to us he gives him a third of what is in his hand.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the acknowledgment of a bequest by an heir after the division of the estate. The text begins by distinguishing between consecutive and simultaneous acknowledgments. If an heir acknowledges a bequest for one person, then later acknowledges for another consecutively, the first acknowledgment takes priority and the entire third is given to the first. However, if the acknowledgments are simultaneous (connected), the third is divided equally between the two. The author draws an analogy to the acknowledgment of a deposit. Then the text discusses cases where the heir acknowledges a specific item vs. a share. The key principle is that an heir's acknowledgment only binds himself and does not affect the shares of other heirs. This is contrasted with acknowledgment of a debt, which takes priority over inheritance. The Sharh then presents a case from al-Kafi where two sons divided an estate and one acknowledges a bequest of one-third. According to istihsan (the Hanafi majority view), the acknowledging son gives one-third of his share to the legatee. Zufr argues by qiyas that he should give half, reasoning that the acknowledgment implies equality between the sons, so the legatee should take half of the acknowledging son's share. The Hanafi response is that the acknowledgment is only for a third of the total estate, not for equality, and the denying son's share is not affected. The same reasoning applies to cases with more sons. The relied-upon position is the istihsan view.

Key Terms
الإقرار (al-iqrar): An heir's admission of a bequest made by the testator.
الثلث (al-thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum portion that can be bequeathed to non-heirs.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference used to override qiyas in this ruling.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning applied by Zufr to derive the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi majority, how much does an acknowledging son give to a legatee when he acknowledges his father's bequest of one-third after the estate has been divided?
A) One-third of the son's share
B) Half of the son's share
C) One-third of the total estate
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The principle of iqrar yasarr (acknowledgment binds only the acknowledger) ensures that a legatee receives exactly one-third of the acknowledging heir's share, not more.

Ruling on Bequest of Another's Property with Owner's Ratification
Ruling on bequest of another's property with owner ratification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a bequest of a specific item from another's property when the owner ratifies, and explain the owner's right to refuse delivery after ratification.

Core Idea
A bequest of another's property is valid upon the owner's ratification, but the owner may still refuse delivery because ratification is a new revocable gift.

In Hanafi law, a bequest of property belonging to another person is suspended on the owner's ratification after the testator's death. This passage explains that if the owner ratifies and delivers the item, the bequest is valid, yet the owner retains the right to refuse delivery. Understanding this distinction is crucial for differentiating between ratification of a bequest of another's property and ratification by heirs of impermissible bequests.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Initial Suspension
The testator bequeaths a specific item (e.g., 1000 dirhams) that belongs to someone else. This bequest is suspended (mawquf) on the owner's ratification after the testator's death because it is a gift (tabarru') of another's property.
The bequest is not initially valid because the testator does not own the item.
2
Understand the Effect of Ratification
When the owner ratifies and delivers the item, the bequest becomes valid (sahih). However, the ratification is considered a new gift initiated by the owner, not an extension of the testator's bequest.
The owner's ratification is a fresh act of giving.
3
Recognize the Owner's Right to Refuse Delivery
Because the ratification is a new gift, the owner retains the right to revoke it before delivery (qabd). This is consistent with the general rule that voluntary gifts can be revoked before delivery.
Contrast with sales, which are binding upon contract.
4
Distinguish from Heirs' Ratification of Impermissible Bequests
When the testator bequeaths an excess over one-third or to an heir, and the heirs ratify, they cannot later refuse delivery because the bequest itself was valid in essence—it was only prevented by their right. Their ratification removes that obstacle, so the bequest is executed from the testator's estate.
The difference lies in the validity of the underlying bequest: in the first case, the testator did not own the item; in the second, he did.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وبألف عين من مال آخر فأجاز رب المال بعد موت الموصي ودفعه صح وله المنع بعد الاجازة) أي إذا اوصى لرجل بألف درهم بعينها من مال غيره فأجاز صاحب المال بعد موت الموصي ودفعه إليه جاز وله الامتناع من التسليم بعد الاجازة لأنه تبرع بمال الغير فيتوقف على إجازة صاحبه فإن أجاز كان منه هذا إبتداء فله أن يمتنع من التسليم كسائر التبرعات بخلاف ما إذا أوصى بالزيادة على الثلث أو للقاتل أو للوارث فأجازتها الورثة حيث لا يكون لهم أن يمنعوا من التسليم لأن الوصية تبرع في نفسها صحيحة لمصادفتها ملكه وإنما امتنع لحق الورثة فإذا اجازوها سقط حقهم فتنفذ من جهة الموصي على ما بيناه من قبل؛ كذا ذكر الشارح .
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And with a specific thousand from another's wealth, so if the owner ratifies after the death of the testator and delivers it, it is valid, and he has the right to refuse after ratification.) That is, if he bequeaths to a man a specific thousand dirhams from the wealth of another, and the owner ratifies after the death of the testator and delivers it to him, it is valid, and he has the right to refuse delivery after ratification, because it is a gift of another's wealth, so it is suspended on the owner's ratification. If he ratifies, it becomes from him as an initiation, so he may refuse delivery like all other gifts. Unlike when he bequeaths an excess over the third or to the killer or to the heir, and the heirs ratify it, where they do not have the right to refuse delivery, because the bequest in itself is valid, as it coincides with his ownership, but it was prevented due to the right of the heirs. When they ratify, their right falls, so it is executed from the testator's side as we explained before. Thus mentioned the commentator.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage explains a ruling from the matn regarding a bequest of a specific item that belongs to another person. If a testator bequeaths a specific thousand dirhams from someone else's property, the bequest is suspended on the owner's ratification after the testator's death. If the owner ratifies and delivers it, the bequest is valid, but the owner may still refuse to deliver after ratifying because his ratification is considered a new gift from him, and he has the right to revoke a gift before delivery. This is in contrast to cases where the testator bequeaths an amount exceeding the one-third or bequeaths to an heir or to the killer of the testator; in those cases, if the heirs ratify, the ratification is effective and they cannot later refuse because the bequest itself was valid in essence but was prevented by the heirs' right. Once they waive that right, the bequest is executed from the testator's estate.

Key Terms
الألف بعينها (al-alf bi'-aynihi): The specific one thousand dirhams being bequeathed.
الإجازة (al-ijazah): The owner's ratification of the bequest after the testator's death.
التبرع (al-tabarru'): A voluntary gift or donation.
الامتناع من التسليم (al-imtina' min al-taslim): The right to refuse delivery after ratification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No, ratification makes it binding
B) Yes, because the ratification is a new gift and gifts can be revoked before delivery
C) No, because the testator's bequest is valid
D) Yes, only if the testator was not the owner

Key Takeaway
A bequest of another's specific property is valid upon owner ratification, but the owner can still refuse delivery because the ratification is treated as a new revocable gift.

Acknowledgment of Bequest: Istihsan vs Qiyas After Division
Intra-Hanafi dispute on amount owed by acknowledging son

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on an acknowledging son's liability after estate division and evaluate the istihsan vs qiyas arguments within the school.

Core Idea
Istihsan overrides qiyas: an acknowledging son gives only one-third of his share, not half, because his acknowledgment binds only himself.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: when one of two sons acknowledges a bequest after the estate has been divided, how much must he give the legatee? The matn states one-third, but Zufr argues by qiyas that half is required. We will trace the reasoning behind both positions and see why the majority prefers istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and scenario
There are two sons who have divided their father's estate. One son later acknowledges that their father bequeathed one-third to a third party. What is the acknowledging son's liability?
Assume no evidence, only acknowledgment.
2
State the Zahir al-Riwayah position
According to the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), the son gives one-third of his own share. This is based on istihsan (juristic preference).
The ruling is wajib on the acknowledging son.
3
Analyze Zufr's qiyas argument
Zufr argues by qiyas: acknowledging a third implies the son admits equality with his brother, so to restore equality he should give half. He compares it to acknowledging a third brother, where the share is split equally.
Zufr treats the acknowledgment as an admission of equality.
4
Evaluate the istihsan response
The Hanafi majority responds that acknowledgment only binds the acknowledger. He only admits a one-third share in the whole estate, not equality. Also, giving half could cause the legatee to receive more than one-third of the total if the other son also acknowledges, violating the one-third limit.
The analogy with a third brother is rejected because that involves equality by nature.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under the majority, the legatee gets 1/3 of the acknowledging son's share; under Zufr, he gets 1/2.
The majority view is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وصح اقرار أحد الابنين بعد القسمة بوصية أبيه في ثلث نصيبه) معناه إذا قسم الابنان تركة أبيهما وهي ألف درهم مثلاً ثم أقر أحدهما لرجل أن أباه أوصى له بثلث ماله فإن المقر يعطيه ثلث ما في يده وهذا استحسان والقياس يعطيه نصف ما في يده وهو قول زفر لإن إقراره بالثلث له تضمن إقراره بمساواته إياه والتسوية في إعطاء النصف ليبقى له النصف فصار كما إذا أقر أحدهما بأخ ثالث لهما، وهذا لأن ما أخذه المنكر كالهالك فيهلك عليهما. وجه الاستحسان إنه أقر له بثلث شائع في جميع التركة وهي في أيديهما فيكون مقراً له بثلث ما في يده وبثلث ما في يد أخيه فيقبل إقراره في حق نفسه ولا يقبل في حق أخيه لعدم الولاية عليه فيعطيه ثلث ما في يده، ولأنه لو أخذ منه نصف ما في يده أدى إلى محظور وهو أن الابن الآخر ربما يقربه فيأخذ نصف ما في يده فيأخذ نصف التركة فيزداد نصيبه على الثلث وهو خلف وقيدنا بالوصية ليحرز عن الدين قال بخلاف ما إذا أقر أحدهما بالدين على أبيهما حيث يأخذ صاحب الدين المقر له جميع ما في يد المقر حتى يستوفي دينه ولا شيء للمقر إن لم يفضل منه شيء لأن الدين مقدم على الميراث فيكون مقراً بتقديمه عليه فيقدم عليه ولا كذلك الوصية لأن الموصى له شريك للورثة فلا يأخذ شيئاً إلا إذا سلم للوارث ضعف ذلك ولا نسلم أنه أقر له بالمساواة بل أقر له بثلث التركة وإنما حصلت المساواة باتفاق الحال ولهذا لو لم يكن له أخ فأقر له بالوصية لا يزيد حقه على الثلث ولو كان مقراً بالمساواة لمساواة حالة الانفراد أيضاً بخلاف ما إذا أقر بأخ ثالث وكذبه أخوه حيث يكون ما في يد المقر بينهما نصفين لأنه أقر له بالمساواة فيساويه مطلقاً، ولهذا لو كان وحده إيضاً ساواه فيكون ما أخذه المنكر هالكاً عليهما .اهـ. كلام الشارح وهذا حيث لا بينة، وأما إذا كان إقرار وبينة قال في المبسوط أقر أن فلاناً أوصى لفلان بالثلث وقامت البينة لأخر يدفع إليه ولا يضمن الوارث شيئاً لأن الشهادة حجة على الكافة والإقرار حجة قاصرة على المقر وليس بحجة في حق المشهود له فثبتت وصية المشهود له في حق المقر له ولم تثبت وصية المقر له في حق المشهود له فيكون هو أولى باستحقاق الثلث من المقر له كما لو أقر ذو اليد بالدار لرجل وأقام الآخر البينة على أنها ملكه يقضى بها للمشهود له فكذا هذا .
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And the acknowledgment of one of the two sons after division of the bequest of their father regarding a third of his share is valid.) Its meaning: if the two sons divide their father's estate, which is one thousand dirhams for example, then one of them acknowledges to a man that his father bequeathed to him a third of his wealth, then the acknowledger gives him a third of what is in his hand. This is istihsan. By qiyas, he would give him half of what is in his hand, and this is the saying of Zufr, because his acknowledgment of the third for him implies his acknowledgment of his equality with him, and the equality requires giving half so that half remains for him. So it becomes as if one of them acknowledged a third brother for them. This is because what the denier takes is like lost, so it is lost to both. The face of istihsan is that he acknowledged for him a third share in the entire estate, and it is in their hands, so he is acknowledging for him a third of what is in his hand and a third of what is in his brother's hand. So his acknowledgment is accepted regarding his own right, and not accepted regarding his brother's right due to lack of authority over him, so he gives him a third of what is in his hand. Also, if he took from him half of what is in his hand, it would lead to a prohibited outcome: the other son might possibly take [the legatee?] and he would take half of what is in his hand, so he would take half of the estate, thus his share would increase beyond the third, which is a contradiction. And we restricted it to bequest to differentiate from debt. He said: unlike if one of them acknowledges a debt on their father, where the creditor takes all that is in the hand of the acknowledger until his debt is satisfied, and there is nothing for the acknowledger if nothing remains, because the debt takes precedence over inheritance, so he is acknowledging its precedence over him, so it takes precedence. Not so for bequest, because the legatee is a partner with the heirs, so he takes nothing unless the heir is left with double that. And we do not concede that he acknowledged equality; rather, he acknowledged a third of the estate. Equality only occurred by chance of the situation. For this, if he had no brother and he acknowledged the bequest, his right does not exceed the third. If he were acknowledging equality, it would also be equal in the case of solitude. Unlike if he acknowledged a third brother and his brother denied him, where what is in the hand of the acknowledger is divided between them in halves, because he acknowledged equality, so he equals him absolutely. For this, if he were alone, he would also equal him. So what the denier takes is lost to both. End of the commentator's words. This is where there is no evidence. As for when there is acknowledgment and evidence, he said in al-Mabsut: if he acknowledged that so-and-so bequeathed to so-and-so the third, and evidence was established for another, it is given to him, and the heir is not liable for anything, because testimony is a proof against everyone, while acknowledgment is a limited proof against the acknowledger only, and it is not a proof in the right of the one testified for. So the bequest of the one testified for is established in the right of the acknowledged, and the bequest of the acknowledged is not established in the right of the one testified for, so he is more entitled to the third than the acknowledged one. Just as if the possessor acknowledged the house to a man, and another established evidence that it is his property, it is judged for the one with evidence. So is this.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage further elaborates on the ruling of an heir's acknowledgment after division, now specifically for one of two sons. The matn states that such acknowledgment is valid regarding the son's own share. The commentary explains that the acknowledging son gives one-third of his share by istihsan, while Zufr argues by qiyas that he should give half. The majority view is based on the principle that acknowledgment only binds the acknowledger. The text then distinguishes this from acknowledgment of a debt, which takes priority over inheritance. The passage also discusses the effect of evidence: if there is a conflict between an acknowledgment and evidence, the evidence prevails because it is a universal proof. This is illustrated by the analogy of a house claimed by two people, one with acknowledgment and one with evidence.

Key Terms
الإقرار (al-iqrar): An heir's admission of a bequest made by the testator.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference used to derive the ruling of giving one-third.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning used by Zufr to argue for half.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One-third of his own share
B) Half of his own share
C) One-third of the total estate
D) Nothing, because the other son denies

Key Takeaway
When one heir acknowledges a bequest after division, he gives one-third of his own share by istihsan, not half by qiyas, because acknowledgment only binds the acknowledger.

Precedence of Evidence over Acknowledgment in Bequest Claims
Ruling on evidence overriding acknowledgment in bequest claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that evidence overrides acknowledgment in bequest disputes and explain the distinction between bequest and debt regarding priority.

Core Idea
Evidence is a proof for all; acknowledgment is only against the acknowledger, so evidence prevails in conflicts.

The previous lesson assumed no evidence. Now the passage addresses a scenario where there is both an acknowledgment and evidence from a different claimant. The rule is clear: evidence (bayyinah) takes precedence over acknowledgment because it is a universal proof (hujjah 'ala al-kafah), whereas acknowledgment is a limited proof (hujjah qasirah). This lesson also contrasts bequest with debt, where debt takes priority over inheritance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario with evidence
One son acknowledges a bequest to X, but Y brings evidence (witnesses) that the bequest was to him. How does the judge decide?
Assume both claim the same one-third bequest.
2
State the ruling: evidence prevails
The judge gives the bequest to Y (the one with evidence) because testimony is a universal proof. The acknowledging son is not liable to X because his acknowledgment is only against himself and not against Y.
This is analogous to a possessor of a house acknowledging ownership to one person while another provides evidence of ownership.
3
Understand the analogy with a house
If a person in possession of a house acknowledges it belongs to A, but B brings evidence it is his, the judge rules for B. Similarly here, the legatee with evidence takes priority.
The universal proof overrides the limited one.
4
Contrast with debt
If the claim were a debt instead of a bequest, the acknowledging son would be liable to the creditor because debt takes precedence over inheritance. The creditor can take the acknowledging son's entire share until the debt is paid.
Bequest is different: the legatee is a partner with the heirs, not a creditor with priority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وصح اقرار أحد الابنين بعد القسمة بوصية أبيه في ثلث نصيبه) معناه إذا قسم الابنان تركة أبيهما وهي ألف درهم مثلاً ثم أقر أحدهما لرجل أن أباه أوصى له بثلث ماله فإن المقر يعطيه ثلث ما في يده وهذا استحسان والقياس يعطيه نصف ما في يده وهو قول زفر لإن إقراره بالثلث له تضمن إقراره بمساواته إياه والتسوية في إعطاء النصف ليبقى له النصف فصار كما إذا أقر أحدهما بأخ ثالث لهما، وهذا لأن ما أخذه المنكر كالهالك فيهلك عليهما. وجه الاستحسان إنه أقر له بثلث شائع في جميع التركة وهي في أيديهما فيكون مقراً له بثلث ما في يده وبثلث ما في يد أخيه فيقبل إقراره في حق نفسه ولا يقبل في حق أخيه لعدم الولاية عليه فيعطيه ثلث ما في يده، ولأنه لو أخذ منه نصف ما في يده أدى إلى محظور وهو أن الابن الآخر ربما يقربه فيأخذ نصف ما في يده فيأخذ نصف التركة فيزداد نصيبه على الثلث وهو خلف وقيدنا بالوصية ليحرز عن الدين قال بخلاف ما إذا أقر أحدهما بالدين على أبيهما حيث يأخذ صاحب الدين المقر له جميع ما في يد المقر حتى يستوفي دينه ولا شيء للمقر إن لم يفضل منه شيء لأن الدين مقدم على الميراث فيكون مقراً بتقديمه عليه فيقدم عليه ولا كذلك الوصية لأن الموصى له شريك للورثة فلا يأخذ شيئاً إلا إذا سلم للوارث ضعف ذلك ولا نسلم أنه أقر له بالمساواة بل أقر له بثلث التركة وإنما حصلت المساواة باتفاق الحال ولهذا لو لم يكن له أخ فأقر له بالوصية لا يزيد حقه على الثلث ولو كان مقراً بالمساواة لمساواة حالة الانفراد أيضاً بخلاف ما إذا أقر بأخ ثالث وكذبه أخوه حيث يكون ما في يد المقر بينهما نصفين لأنه أقر له بالمساواة فيساويه مطلقاً، ولهذا لو كان وحده إيضاً ساواه فيكون ما أخذه المنكر هالكاً عليهما .اهـ. كلام الشارح وهذا حيث لا بينة، وأما إذا كان إقرار وبينة قال في المبسوط أقر أن فلاناً أوصى لفلان بالثلث وقامت البينة لأخر يدفع إليه ولا يضمن الوارث شيئاً لأن الشهادة حجة على الكافة والإقرار حجة قاصرة على المقر وليس بحجة في حق المشهود له فثبتت وصية المشهود له في حق المقر له ولم تثبت وصية المقر له في حق المشهود له فيكون هو أولى باستحقاق الثلث من المقر له كما لو أقر ذو اليد بالدار لرجل وأقام الآخر البينة على أنها ملكه يقضى بها للمشهود له فكذا هذا .
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And the acknowledgment of one of the two sons after division of the bequest of their father regarding a third of his share is valid.) The face of istihsan is that he acknowledged for him a third share in the entire estate, and it is in their hands, so he is acknowledging for him a third of what is in his hand and a third of what is in his brother's hand. So his acknowledgment is accepted regarding his own right, and not accepted regarding his brother's right due to lack of authority over him, so he gives him a third of what is in his hand. Also, if he took from him half of what is in his hand, it would lead to a prohibited outcome: the other son might possibly take [the legatee?] and he would take half of what is in his hand, so he would take half of the estate, thus his share would increase beyond the third, which is a contradiction. And we do not concede that he acknowledged equality; rather, he acknowledged a third of the estate. Equality only occurred by chance of the situation. So the bequest of the one testified for is established in the right of the acknowledged, and the bequest of the acknowledged is not established in the right of the one testified for, so he is more entitled to the third than the acknowledged one. Just as if the possessor acknowledged the house to a man, and another established evidence that it is his property, it is judged for the one with evidence. So is this.

This passage further elaborates on the ruling of an heir's acknowledgment after division, now specifically for one of two sons. The matn states that such acknowledgment is valid regarding the son's own share. الشهادة (al-shahadah): Testimony given by witnesses in court.

One Son's Acknowledgment of Father's Will After Division
Ruling on acknowledgment of bequest after division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on one son's acknowledgment of a will after division and explain why istihsan is preferred over qiyas.

Core Idea
An acknowledgment only binds the one who makes it — so the son gives only from his own share, not half.

In this lesson, you will learn about a specific case in inheritance law: when one of two sons acknowledges a bequest after dividing the estate. The Hanafi ruling, based on istihsan, holds that the acknowledging son must give only one-third of his share to the legatee. We will explore why this differs from qiyas (which would require half) and from the case of debt, and how the hierarchy of proofs resolves the dispute.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
Two sons divide the father's estate equally. Later, one son acknowledges that his father bequeathed one-third of the entire estate to a non-heir. Identify the parties and the amounts.
The acknowledgment occurs after division, so each son already has his share.
2
Identify the two rulings
The text presents two rulings: the istihsan ruling (give one-third of the acknowledging son's share) and the qiyas ruling (give half). Note which is the dominant Hanafi position and which is Zufar's.
Istihsan is the mufta bihi (operative) view.
3
Analyze the istihsan reasoning
The acknowledgment is only binding on the acknowledging son, not on his brother, because he has no authority over his brother's share. Therefore, he only gives from his own portion. The one-third is because he acknowledged a one-third share in the whole estate, but that share is partially in his brother's hand. He cannot affect his brother's portion, so he compensates for the portion in his own hand only.
The principle: iqrar is a proof limited to the declarant.
4
Contrast with debt acknowledgment
If the acknowledgment were for a debt owed by the father, the creditor takes precedence over inheritance and can take the entire share of the acknowledging son. Bequests are different because the legatee is a partner with heirs.
Debt is superior to inheritance; bequest is subordinate.
5
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Given a new set of numbers, calculate how much the acknowledging son must give. For example, if the estate is 60,000, each son gets 30,000. The acknowledging son gives 1/3 of his share = 10,000.
Ensure the legatee is a non-heir; if an heir, different rules apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح اقرار أحد الابنين بعد القسمة بوصية أبيه في ثلث نصيبه معناه إذا قسم الابنان تركة أبيهما وهي ألف درهم مثلاً ثم أقر أحدهما لرجل أن أباه أوصى له بثلث ماله فإن المقر يعطيه ثلث ما في يده وهذا استحسان والقياس يعطيه نصف ما في يده وهو قول زفر لإن إقراره بالثلث له تضمن إقراره بمساواته إياه والتسوية في إعطاء النصف ليبقى له النصف فصار كما إذا أقر أحدهما بأخ ثالث لهما، وهذا لأن ما أخذه المنكر كالهالك فيهلك عليهما. وجه الاستحسان إنه أقر له بثلث شائع في جميع التركة وهي في أيديهما فيكون مقراً له بثلث ما في يده وبثلث ما في يد أخيه فيقبل إقراره في حق نفسه ولا يقبل في حق أخيه لعدم الولاية عليه فيعطيه ثلث ما في يده، ولأنه لو أخذ منه نصف ما في يده أدى إلى محظور وهو أن الابن الآخر ربما يقربه فيأخذ نصف ما في يده فيأخذ نصف التركة فيزداد نصيبه على الثلث وهو خلف وقيدنا بالوصية ليحرز عن الدين قال بخلاف ما إذا أقر أحدهما بالدين على أبيهما حيث يأخذ صاحب الدين المقر له جميع ما في يد المقر حتى يستوفي دينه ولا شيء للمقر إن لم يفضل منه شيء لأن الدين مقدم على الميراث فيكون مقراً بتقديمه عليه فيقدم عليه ولا كذلك الوصية لأن الموصى له شريك للورثة فلا يأخذ شيئاً إلا إذا سلم للوارث ضعف ذلك ولا نسلم أنه أقر له بالمساواة بل أقر له بثلث التركة وإنما حصلت المساواة باتفاق الحال ولهذا لو لم يكن له أخ فأقر له بالوصية لا يزيد حقه على الثلث ولو كان مقراً بالمساواة لمساواة حالة الانفراد أيضاً بخلاف ما إذا أقر بأخ ثالث وكذبه أخوه حيث يكون ما في يد المقر بينهما نصفين لأنه أقر له بالمساواة فيساويه مطلقاً، ولهذا لو كان وحده إيضاً ساواه فيكون ما أخذه المنكر هالكاً عليهما .اهـ. كلام الشارح وهذا حيث لا بينة، وأما إذا كان إقرار وبينة قال في المبسوط أقر أن فلاناً أوصى لفلان بالثلث وقامت البينة لأخر يدفع إليه ولا يضمن الوارث شيئاً لأن الشهادة حجة على الكافة والإقرار حجة قاصرة على المقر وليس بحجة في حق المشهود له فثبتت وصية المشهود له في حق المقر له ولم تثبت وصية المقر له في حق المشهود له فيكون هو أولى باستحقاق الثلث من المقر له كما لو أقر ذو اليد بالدار لرجل وأقام الآخر البينة على أنها ملكه يقضى بها للمشهود له فكذا هذا
And it is valid for one of the two sons after division to acknowledge his father's bequest of one-third of his share: meaning if the two sons divided their father's estate, e.g., one thousand dirhams, then one of them acknowledged to a man that his father bequeathed him one-third of his property, then the acknowledging one gives him one-third of what is in his hand. This is istihsan, and by qiyas he would give him half of what is in his hand, which is Zufar's opinion, because his acknowledgment of one-third for him implies his acknowledgment of equality with him, and equality requires giving half so that half remains for him, thus it becomes as if one of them acknowledged a third brother, and this is because what the denier takes is like lost property that is lost to both. The basis of istihsan is that he acknowledged for him a one-third share in the entire estate, which is in their hands, so he is acknowledging for him one-third of what is in his hand and one-third of what is in his brother's hand. His acknowledgment is accepted regarding himself but not regarding his brother due to lack of authority over him, so he gives him one-third of what is in his hand. Also, if he took half of what is in his hand, it would lead to a prohibited outcome: that the other son might also make him take half of what is in his hand, thus taking half the estate, increasing his share above one-third, which is contrary to the condition. And we restricted it to a bequest to distinguish it from a debt. He said: unlike if one of them acknowledged a debt owed by their father, where the creditor takes all that is in the hand of the acknowledging one until his debt is paid, and nothing remains for the acknowledging one if nothing is left, because debt takes precedence over inheritance, so he is acknowledging its precedence over him, thus it is given priority. But not so with a bequest, because the legatee is a partner with the heirs, so he takes nothing unless the heir receives double that. And we do not concede that he acknowledged equality; rather he acknowledged one-third of the estate, and equality only occurs by coincidence of circumstances. Hence, if he had no brother and acknowledged the bequest, his right does not exceed one-third; if he were acknowledging equality, it would be equal even in the case of being alone. This is unlike if he acknowledged a third brother and his brother denied, where what is in the acknowledging one's hand is divided between them in halves, because he acknowledged equality, so he is equal absolutely. Hence, even if alone, he equals him, and what the denier takes is lost to both. End of the commentator's words. This is when there is no evidence. As for when there is an acknowledgment and evidence, it is stated in al-Mabsut: if he acknowledged that so-and-so bequeathed to so-and-so one-third, and evidence was established for another, he gives it to him, and the heir does not guarantee anything, because testimony is a proof binding on all, while acknowledgment is a limited proof binding only on the acknowledging one and is not a proof against the one for whom testimony is given. Thus the bequest of the one with testimony is established against the one who acknowledged, and the bequest of the one who acknowledged is not established against the one with testimony, so he is more entitled to the one-third than the acknowledging one, just as if the possessor of a house acknowledged it for a man and another established evidence that it is his, the judgment is given to the one with evidence. The same applies here.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling on one of two sons acknowledging a bequest after dividing the estate. The commentator begins by stating the operative ruling: it is valid for one son to acknowledge a bequest, and he must give one-third of his own share (not half) to the legatee. This ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference), while qiyas (analogy) would require half. The author then contrasts the positions: Zufar holds the qiyas view, arguing that acknowledging one-third implies equality, so half should be given. The Hanafi position rejects this, explaining that the acknowledgment is only binding on the acknowledging person, not on his brother, because he has no authority over his brother's share. Therefore, he gives only from his own portion. The text also distinguishes between a bequest and a debt: in a debt, the creditor takes priority and can take the entire share of the acknowledging heir because debt is superior to inheritance. The passage further clarifies that if one heir acknowledges and the other denies, and there is also evidence (bayyinah) supporting a different claimant, the one with evidence prevails over the one who only has an acknowledgment. This shows the hierarchy of proofs: testimony is binding on all, while acknowledgment only binds the one who makes it.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or admission by a person of a right belonging to another. In this context, one son's acknowledgment of a bequest made by the father.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that departs from strict analogy to avoid hardship or achieve a fairer outcome. Here, it leads to giving one-third instead of half.
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A bequest or will, typically limited to one-third of the estate for non-heirs.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning. Here, Zufar uses qiyas to equate acknowledgment of a bequest with acknowledgment of a brother.
بينة (bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically testimony of witnesses. In the passage, it is contrasted with iqrar as a stronger proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the istihsan ruling, how much does the acknowledging son give to the legatee?
A) Half of his share
B) The entire share
C) One-third of his share
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, one son's acknowledgment of a bequest after division only obligates him to give one-third of his own share, based on istihsan, not half as qiyas would suggest.

Bequest of a Slave-Girl and Her Posthumous Child: Hanafi Ruling and Intra-School Dispute
Ruling on a bequeathed slave-girl who gives birth after the testator's death and the allocation of the one-third.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the bequest of a slave-girl who gives birth after the testator's death, explain the condition regarding the one-third, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The increase (child) born after death follows the bequest if it fits within one-third; otherwise, the mother is taken first.

Bequests are limited to one-third of the estate, and increases occurring after death can complicate matters. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a specific scenario: a slave-girl bequeathed to someone gives birth after the testator's death. The ruling hinges on whether both mother and child can be accommodated within the one-third. We will unpack the rule, the underlying principle of 'the estate remains on the deceased's ownership until division,' and the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the opening sentence. The ruling states that if both the mother and child come out of the one-third, both belong to the legatee. If not, the legatee takes the mother first, and any remainder from the one-third goes to the child.
This is Abu Hanifa's position.
2
Understand the condition of timing
The passage specifies that the birth must occur before division of the estate and before the legatee accepts the bequest. The increase (child) is considered part of the estate because the estate remains on the deceased's ownership until division.
If born after acceptance, the increase might not follow the bequest.
3
Trace the usul principle
The commentator explains that the estate before division is treated as still belonging to the deceased. Any increase (like a child, earnings, or blood money) is part of the estate and subject to bequests and debts. This is analogized to a sold item before delivery.
This is a talil (reasoning) based on the analogy of sale.
4
Contrast with the Sahibayn's view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the one-third should be distributed proportionally between mother and child, not prioritizing the mother. Understand their reasoning: both are equally part of the bequest.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
5
Apply the ruling to a hypothetical
Take a concrete example: estate 1200, one-third = 400. If mother valued at 300, child at 100, both fit, so both go to legatee. If mother 350, child 100, total 450 exceeds one-third, legatee takes mother (350) and only 50 from child's value.
Practice the calculation.

قال رحمه الله : (وبأمة فولدت بعد موته وخرجا من ثلثه فهما له وإلا أخذ منها ثم منه) أي إذا أوصى لرجل بجارية فولدت بعد موت الموصي ولداً وكلاهما يخرجان من الثلث فهما للموصى له لأن الأم دخلت في الوصية أصالة والولد تابع حين كان متصلاً بها، وعبارته صادقة بما إذا ولدت قبل القبول والقسمة، فلو قال فولدت بعدهما إلى آخره لكان أولى لأنها إذا ولدت قبل القسمة والتركة مبقاة على ملك الميت قبلها حتى يقضي منها ديونه وتنفذ وصاياه دخل ولدها في الوصية فيكونان للموصى له، وإن لم يخرجا من الثلث أخذ ما يخصه من الأم أولاً، فإن فضل شيء أخذه من الولد وهذا عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما يعطى له الثلث منهما بالحصص. قال الشارح وعبارة المؤلف صادقة بما إذا حدثت قبل القبول أو بعده قال في المبسوط : أصله أن التركة قبل القسمة مبقاة على حكم الميت حتى إن الزيادة الحادثة قبل القسمة تعد من مال الميت حتى يقضي دينه وتنفذ وصاياه لأن الموصى له والورثة تتملك والوصية من جهة الميت فيعتبر بما لو ملك المال من غيره بالبيع أو بالنكاح، والزوائد الحادثة من المبيع والمهر قبل القبض حادثة على ملك المالك الثمن بالقبض لأن ما يملك يكون مبقى على ملك المملك فكذا هذا. وظاهر قوله قبل القسمة أنها بعد القسمة ليست بمبقاة فتكون الزوائد للموصى له . ثم المسائل على فصلين: أحدهما في الزيادة والثاني في النقصان والزيادة الحادثة من الموصى به كالولد والغلة والكسب والأرش بعد موت الموصي قبل قبول الموصى له الوصية يصير موصى بها حتى تعتبر من الثلث لأنها حدثت بعد انعقاد سبب الملك للموصى له في الأصل، فإذا حدثت الملك فيه إلى وقت الموت تدخل تحت الوصية كالمبيعة إذا ولدت في مدة بسبب الخيار واختار من له الخيار البيع فتصير الزيادة مبيعة حتى تصير لها حصة من الثمن، فأما إذا حدثت قبل الموصى له قبل القسمة هل يصير موصى بها ؟ لم يذكره محمد وذكر القدوري أنه لا يصير موصى بها حتى كانت للموصى المال كما لو حدثت بعد القسمة لأن الزيادة حدثت بعد ملك الموصى له وبعد تأكد ملكه لأنه ملك الرقبة وتصرف فيه جميعاً فصار كالزيادة الحادثة المبيعة بعد القبض . وقال مشايخنا يصير موصى بها حتى يعتبر خروجها من الثلث لأنها حدثت بعد الملك قبل تأكد الملك في الأصل لأن ملكه لم يتأكد ولم يتقرر بعد لأنه لو هلك ثلث التركة وصارت الحادثة بحيث لا تخرج من ثلث ماله يكون من الحادثة بقدر ثلث الباقي فصار كالزيادة الممهورة الحادثة قبل القبض تصير مهراً حتى تسقط بالطلاق قبل الدخول وقد ملكت الرقبة والتصرف جميعاً لأن ملكها غير متأكد قبل القبض حتى لو هلك هلك على الزوج لا عليها ثم الحق الكسب يرد عليه مقصوداً لهما أن الزيادة متى حدثت قبل القبض تصير موصى بها حكماً. ولأبي حنيفة أن الحادث قبل القبض صار مقصوداً لكنه تبعاً لا أصلاً، وهذا لبيان أنها كانت باقية على ملك الميت فلو تصرف فيه الوارث صح
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And regarding a slave-girl who gave birth after his death and both come out of his one-third, then both belong to him; otherwise, he takes from her first, then from him). That is, if a man bequeaths a slave-girl to someone, and she gives birth after the testator's death, and both come out of the one-third, then both belong to the legatee, because the mother entered the bequest as principal and the child is a follower since it was connected to her. And his expression is inclusive of when she gave birth before acceptance and division. If he said 'she gave birth after them' to the end, it would be better, because if she gives birth before division and the estate is kept on the deceased's ownership until debts are paid and bequests executed, her child enters the bequest, so both belong to the legatee. If both do not come out of the one-third, he takes what is his share from the mother first; if anything remains, he takes from the child. This is according to Abu Hanifa. According to the two companions, he is given one-third from both proportionally. The commentator said: The author's expression is valid for when it occurs before acceptance or after. He said in al-Mabsut: The principle is that the estate before division remains in the status of the deceased's property, so that any increase occurring before division is considered part of the deceased's estate, until his debts are paid and his bequests executed, because the legatee and heirs acquire ownership, and the bequest is from the deceased. So it is considered like when someone owns property by sale or marriage, and the increments arising from the sold item or dower before receipt arise on the ownership of the seller until receipt takes place, because what is owned remains in the ownership of the one who made it owned. The same applies here. The apparent meaning of ‘before division’ is that after division it is no longer in that status, so increments belong to the legatee. Then the issues are of two types: one increase and the other decrease. The increase arising from the bequest, like a child, produce, earnings, and blood money after the testator's death but before the legatee's acceptance of the bequest, becomes part of the bequest so that it is counted from the one-third, because it occurred after the cause of ownership for the legatee was established in principle. Thus when ownership enters it up to the time of death, it falls under the bequest, like a sold item that gives birth during the option period and the one who has the option chooses the sale, then the increase becomes sold so that it has a share of the price. As for when it occurs after the legatee's ownership but before division, does it become part of the bequest? Muhammad did not mention it, and al-Quduri mentioned that it does not become part of the bequest, and it belongs to the deceased's estate as if it occurred after division, because the increase occurred after the legatee's ownership and after his ownership was confirmed, since he owned both the corpus and the right of disposal, so it becomes like an increase occurring in a sold item after receipt. And our scholars said: It becomes part of the bequest so that its exit from the one-third is considered, because it occurred after ownership but before confirmation of ownership in principle, because his ownership has not been confirmed and established, because if one-third of the estate perishes and the increase is such that it does not come out of the remaining one-third, then from the increase he takes the amount of the remaining one-third. This is like an increase in a dower that occurs before receipt, which becomes part of the dower so that it falls by divorce before consummation, even though the wife owned the corpus and disposal, because her ownership is not confirmed before receipt; if it perishes, it perishes on the husband, not on her. Then, regarding the earnings, they are attached to the child in the bequest but not in a sale, because earnings are in exchange for usufruct, and usufruct can be owned as a purpose through bequest, so its counterpart also can, unlike sale. Thus, earnings cannot be made a sold item as a purpose by the contract of sale because receipt is intended for it. For both, whenever an increase occurs before receipt, it becomes part of the bequest by legal implication. According to Abu Hanifa, what occurs before receipt becomes intended, but as a follower, not as a principal. This is to explain that the estate remained in the deceased's ownership; if the heir disposes of it, it is valid.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage deals with the bequest of a slave-girl who gives birth after the testator's death. The ruling is that if both the mother and the child can be taken from the one-third of the estate, both go to the legatee. Otherwise, the legatee first takes the mother to the extent of his one-third, and if anything remains, he takes from the child. This is Abu Hanifa's view. His two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the one-third is distributed proportionally between the mother and child. The commentator explains that the estate before division is considered as still belonging to the deceased, so any increase (like a child born) is part of the estate and subject to bequest. The key condition is the timing: if the birth occurs before the legatee accepts the bequest and before the estate is divided, the increase enters the bequest. The passage also discusses the difference between a bequest and a sale regarding earnings: in a bequest, earnings from the bequeathed item (like wages from the slave's work) follow the bequest, but in a sale, earnings do not automatically become part of the sale because the purpose of a sale is the corpus, not the earnings. The text further notes that according to the principle, the estate remains on the deceased's ownership until division, so any increase accrues to the estate and is included in the bequest.

Key Terms
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A bequest or will, typically limited to one-third of the estate.
الثلث (al-thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum amount that can be bequeathed to non-heirs without consent of heirs.
الزيادة (al-ziyadah): Increase or increment occurring to the bequeathed property after the testator's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a bequeathed slave-girl gives birth after the testator's death and both mother and child do not come out of the one-third, what is taken first?
A) The child first
B) Both are taken proportionally
C) The mother first, then the child if anything remains
D) Nothing is taken

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the increase (child) of a bequeathed slave-girl born after the testator's death is included in the bequest if it arises before division; if the one-third is insufficient, the mother is taken first (Abu Hanifa).

Sale of Bequeathed Property by Co-owner: Basic Ruling
Basic ruling on sale by co-owner and apportionment of offspring

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sale of a bequeathed slave-girl by an heir when the beneficiary does not ratify, and calculate the shares of the slave-girl and her offspring.

Core Idea
A co-owner's sale is effective only in his own share; the other co-owner's share remains unaffected.

When an heir sells a bequeathed slave-girl without the beneficiary's consent, the sale is not entirely void. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the heir's share and the beneficiary's share. This lesson unpacks the basic scenario where the slave-girl gives birth after the sale, and we determine who gets what.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their ownership shares
The deceased bequeathed one-third of the slave-girl to a beneficiary (musa lahu). The heirs own the remaining two-thirds. So before the sale, the slave-girl is co-owned: heirs 2/3, beneficiary 1/3.
2
Apply the rule for a co-owner's sale
According to Hanafi fiqh, when one co-owner sells shared property without the other's consent, the sale is valid (nafidh) only in the seller's own share. It is void (batil) in the other co-owner's share unless ratified later.
Here, the heir (co-owner of 2/3) sold the whole slave-girl. The sale is effective only in his 2/3 share; the beneficiary's 1/3 remains with the estate.
3
Determine the outcome without ratification
The beneficiary does not ratify the sale. So the buyer keeps only the heir's 2/3. The beneficiary retains his 1/3 share of the slave-girl. The sale in the beneficiary's share is void.
4
Apportion the offspring (walad)
The child was born after the sale. Ownership at birth determines who owns the child. The buyer owned 2/3 of the mother (because the sale was effective there) and the estate (beneficiary's share) owned 1/3. Therefore, 2/3 of the child goes with the mother to the buyer, and 1/3 remains as part of the estate (now the beneficiary's property).
This follows the rule that offspring of a slave-girl belong to the owner at the time of birth.

فأوصى بها لرجل ثم مات فباعها الوارث بغير محضر من الموصى له فولدت في يد المشتري ولداً قيمته ثلاثمائة درهم ثم جاء الموصى له فلم يجز الموصى له البيع سلم للمشتري ثلثي الجارية وثلثي الولد وللموصى له ثلث الجارية وثلث الولد لأن الجارية مشتركة بين الورثة والموصى له وبيع أحد الشريكين لا ينفذ إلا في نصيبه فنفذ البيع في حصة الورثة وهو ثلثا الجارية ولم ينفذ في حصة الموصى له وهو ثلثها فسلم له ثلث الجارية وأربعة أتساع درهم تمام ثلث المال لأن الجارية مشتركة بين المشتري والموصى له ثلثاها للمشتري وثلثها للموصى له فما ضاع على الحصتين وما بقي بقي على الحصتين فللموصى له ثلث الجارية قيمته ثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث لأن المال وحق الموصى له القسمة وقد انتقص من قيمة الجارية ثلثاها فذهب ثلثا حقه وقيمتها في حق الورثة تعتبر يوم البيع لأنه استهلكها الوارث بالبيع فتعتبر قيمتها يوم الاستهلاك، ويوم البيع كانت قيمة ثلثي الجارية مائتي درهم فصار مال الميت مائتين وثلاثة وثلاثين وثلث فللموصى له ثلث وهو سبعة وسبعون وسبعة أتساع درهم قبل الورثة ولم يجعل للموصي أن ينقض البيع فيما بقي من حقه لأنه يؤدي إلى الدور لأن ما نقص فيه كأنه لم يبعه الورثة، وإذا هلك شيء من مال الميت فيحتاج إلى أن ينقص وصيته عن ذلك، وإذا انتقصت بعد البيع بقدر ما انتقصت وصيته، فإذا نفذ البيع عاد حق الموصى له واحتجت إلى النقص فيؤدي إلى ما لا يتناهى وسهم الدور ساقط فلم يكن حق البعض في الابتداء كيلا يؤدي إلى الدور.
So he bequeathed it to a man, then he died, and the heir sold it without the presence of the beneficiary. Then she gave birth in the hand of the buyer to a child worth three hundred dirhams. Then the beneficiary came and did not ratify the sale. The seller is delivered two-thirds of the slave-girl and two-thirds of the child, and the beneficiary has one-third of the slave-girl and one-third of the child, because the slave-girl is shared between the heirs and the beneficiary, and the sale by one co-owner is only effective in his share. So the sale was effective in the share of the heirs, which is two-thirds of the slave-girl, and was not effective in the share of the beneficiary, which is one-third of her. So one-third of the slave-girl is delivered to him. And the increase occurred after the effectiveness of the disposition which ruled division and possession. So two-thirds of the child after the effectiveness of the sale occurred in the ownership of the buyer, so it is not counted from the estate of the deceased, and one-third of it occurred in the ownership of the deceased, so that is from the estate of the deceased. So the estate on that day became two-thirds of the slave-girl, its value two hundred dirhams. And if she had increased in her period so her value became six hundred, then two-thirds of her is safe for the buyer, one-third of her for the beneficiary, and one-third of one-third of her for the heirs, because the estate of the deceased is four hundred because the sale is effective in two-thirds of the slave-girl, so two-thirds of the increase occurred in the ownership of the buyer, so the estate of the deceased remains her value three hundred, and one-third of the increase its value one hundred, so the estate of the deceased becomes four hundred. So one-third of it is for the beneficiary, which is one hundred and thirty-three and one-third, and three hundred from the original slave-girl and thirty-three from the increase, because the value of two-thirds of the slave-girl is two hundred, so one-third of it is one hundred and thirty-three and one-third, and one-third of one-third of it for the heirs is thirty-six and one-third. And if the slave-girl decreased until she became worth one hundred, the beneficiary takes one-third of her and claims from the heirs from her value forty-four and four-ninths dirhams, completing one-third of the estate, because the slave-girl is shared between the buyer and the beneficiary: two-thirds for the buyer, one-third for the beneficiary. Whatever is lost is on both shares, and whatever remains remains on both shares. So the beneficiary has one-third of the slave-girl, its value thirty-three and one-third, because the estate and the right of the beneficiary is division, and two-thirds of the value of the slave-girl decreased, so two-thirds of his right went. And her value regarding the heirs is considered on the day of sale because the heir consumed her by sale, so her value is considered on the day of consumption. On the day of sale, the value of two-thirds of the slave-girl was two hundred dirhams, so the estate of the deceased became two hundred and thirty-three and one-third, so the beneficiary has one-third, which is seventy-seven and seven-ninths dirhams from the heirs. And he does not have the right to annul the sale regarding what remains of his right, because it leads to circular reasoning. Since what decreased in it is as if the heirs did not sell it, and if something of the estate of the deceased is destroyed, then the bequest must be reduced accordingly. And if it decreased after the sale to the extent that his bequest decreased, then if the sale is executed, the right of the beneficiary returns and needs to be reduced, leading to an infinite regress. And the share of circular reasoning is dropped, so the right of some was not established initially to avoid circular reasoning.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling from the chapter on wills, explaining a complex scenario where a testator bequeaths a slave-girl (or property) to someone, then dies. The heir sells the slave-girl without the beneficiary's presence. The slave-girl gives birth after the sale. The beneficiary does not ratify the sale. The ruling gives the buyer two-thirds of the slave-girl and two-thirds of the child, while the beneficiary gets one-third of each. This is because the bequest was of one-third of the estate? Actually the text implies the bequest was of one-third of the property (the slave-girl was part of the estate). The reasoning is that the slave-girl is shared between the heirs (who own two-thirds) and the beneficiary (who owns one-third). When a co-owner sells something, the sale is only effective in his share. So the heir's sale is valid only in his two-thirds share, not in the beneficiary's one-third. The child is born after the sale, so two-thirds of the child belongs to the buyer (since it was born while the two-thirds were in his ownership), and one-third belongs to the estate (since the beneficiary's one-third share was still in the ownership of the deceased's estate). The text then explores scenarios of increase or decrease in value. If the slave-girl's value increases, the shares are recalculated proportionally. If it decreases, the beneficiary is entitled to the full one-third of the original value from the heirs to make up his bequest. The passage ends by explaining why the beneficiary cannot annul the sale to recover his share from the buyer: doing so would lead to circular reasoning (دور) and infinite regress.

Key Terms
الموصى له (al-musa lahu): The person in whose favor a bequest is made; the beneficiary of the will.
الورثة (al-warathah): The legal heirs of the deceased, who inherit the residue of the estate after debts and bequests.
ولد (walad): Offspring of a slave-girl; in this context, a child born to the bequeathed slave-girl after the owner's death.
شريك (sharik): Co-owner; in this passage, the heir and the beneficiary are co-owners of the slave-girl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the share of the beneficiary (musa lahu) in the child born after the heir's sale of the bequeathed slave-girl, if the beneficiary does not ratify?
A) None, because the child belongs entirely to the buyer.
B) One-third, because the beneficiary's ownership share in the mother was one-third at the time of birth.
C) Two-thirds, because the child is part of the estate.
D) One-half, by analogy to partnership.

Key Takeaway
A co-owner's sale is effective only in his own share; the other co-owner's share remains unchanged, and the offspring of a sold slave-girl is apportioned according to ownership at birth.

Increase in Value: Apportioning Appreciation Between Buyer and Beneficiary
Calculation when value increases after partial sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the new shares when the value of a bequeathed property increases after a partial sale by the heir.

Core Idea
Appreciation in value is apportioned according to ownership at the time it occurs.

After the heir's partial sale, if the slave-girl's value increases, we must determine how the appreciation is divided between the buyer and the estate (beneficiary and heirs). This lesson walks through the Hanafi calculation for such a case.

Guided Path
1
Establish the ownership fractions before increase
After the sale and without ratification, the buyer owns 2/3 of the slave-girl, and the estate (including the beneficiary's share and the heirs' residual estate) owns 1/3. Remember that the beneficiary's bequest is one-third of the original estate, but here the estate's 1/3 is held for the beneficiary, but there may be heirs involved? Actually in this scenario, the heirs are the sellers, so their share (2/3) was sold. The estate's remaining 1/3 is the beneficiary's right. So ownership: buyer 2/3, beneficiary 1/3.
The phrase 'مال الميت' refers to the share owned by the estate, which is the beneficiary's 1/3 in this context.
2
Calculate the increase portion
If the slave-girl's value rises from 300 to 600 dirhams, the increase is 300 dirhams. This increase is apportioned according to the ownership at the time the increase occurs. Since the increase occurs after the sale, it is divided: 2/3 to the buyer, 1/3 to the estate.
Thus, the buyer's share appreciates by 200 dirhams, and the estate's share appreciates by 100 dirhams.
3
Compute the total values for each party
Buyer: original 2/3 of 300 = 200, plus 2/3 of increase 200 = 400. Beneficiary: original 1/3 of 300 = 100, plus 1/3 of increase 100 = 200. But the text gives a different calculation: it says the estate becomes 400, and then the bequest (1/3 of estate) is 133.33, and the heirs get the rest. Let's reconcile: The text says 'فصار مال الميت قيمته أربعمائة' meaning the estate (what the beneficiary is entitled to from the estate) is 400? Actually careful: The text describes a two-step process: first, the sale gives the buyer 2/3 of the slave-girl; the remaining 1/3 is the estate. Then the increase occurs: 2/3 of the increase belongs to the buyer, 1/3 to the estate. So the estate's total is the original 1/3 (value 100) plus 1/3 of the increase (100) = 200. But the text says mal al-mayyit becomes 400? Let's read: 'وثلثها للموصى له وثلث ثلثها للورثة'—actually it says the bequest is one-third of the estate? The passage assumes the bequest was of one-third of the slave-girl? Yes, the bequest is of one-third of the slave-girl. So after the sale and appreciation, the beneficiary is entitled to one-third of the estate. So he bequeathed it to a man, then he died, and the heir sold it without the presence of the beneficiary. Then she gave birth in the hand of the buyer to a child worth three hundred dirhams. Then the beneficiary came and did not ratify the sale. The seller is delivered two-thirds of the slave-girl and two-thirds of the child, and the beneficiary has one-third of the slave-girl and one-third of the child, because the slave-girl is shared between the heirs and the beneficiary, and the sale by one co-owner is only effective in his share. So the sale was effective in the share of the heirs, which is two-thirds of the slave-girl, and was not effective in the share of the beneficiary, which is one-third of her. So one-third of the slave-girl is delivered to him. And the increase occurred after the effectiveness of the disposition which ruled division and possession. So two-thirds of the child after the effectiveness of the sale occurred in the ownership of the buyer, so it is not counted from the estate of the deceased, and one-third of it occurred in the ownership of the deceased, so that is from the estate of the deceased. So the beneficiary has one-third of the slave-girl, its value thirty-three and one-third, because the estate and the right of the beneficiary is division, and two-thirds of the value of the slave-girl decreased, so two-thirds of his right went. And her value regarding the heirs is considered on the day of sale because the heir consumed her by sale, so her value is considered on the day of consumption. On the day of sale, the value of two-thirds of the slave-girl was two hundred dirhams, so the estate of the deceased became two hundred and thirty-three and one-third, so the beneficiary has one-third, which is seventy-seven and seven-ninths dirhams from the heirs. And he does not have the right to annul the sale regarding what remains of his right, because it leads to circular reasoning. Since what decreased in it is as if the heirs did not sell it, and if something of the estate of the deceased is destroyed, then the bequest must be reduced accordingly. And if it decreased after the sale to the extent that his bequest decreased, then if the sale is executed, the right of the beneficiary returns and needs to be reduced, leading to an infinite regress. And the share of circular reasoning is dropped, so the right of some was not established initially to avoid circular reasoning.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling from the chapter on wills, explaining a complex scenario where a testator bequeaths a slave-girl (or property) to someone, then dies. The heir sells the slave-girl without the beneficiary's presence. The slave-girl gives birth after the sale. The beneficiary does not ratify the sale. The ruling gives the buyer two-thirds of the slave-girl and two-thirds of the child, while the beneficiary gets one-third of each. This is because the bequest was of one-third of the estate? Actually the text implies the bequest was of one-third of the property (the slave-girl was part of the estate). The reasoning is that the slave-girl is shared between the heirs (who own two-thirds) and the beneficiary (who owns one-third). When a co-owner sells something, the sale is only effective in his share. So the heir's sale is valid only in his two-thirds share, not in the beneficiary's one-third. The child is born after the sale, so two-thirds of the child belongs to the buyer (since it was born while the two-thirds were in his ownership), and one-third belongs to the estate (since the beneficiary's one-third share was still in the ownership of the deceased's estate). The text then explores scenarios of increase or decrease in value. If the slave-girl's value increases, the shares are recalculated proportionally. If it decreases, the beneficiary is entitled to the full one-third of the original value from the heirs to make up his bequest. The passage ends by explaining why the beneficiary cannot annul the sale to recover his share from the buyer: doing so would lead to circular reasoning (دور) and infinite regress.

Key Terms
زيادة (ziyada): Increase or appreciation in value; also may refer to offspring (in the context of slaves).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of increase after sale, what fraction of the increase does the buyer receive?
A) All of it, because the sale transferred ownership.
B) Two-thirds, because the sale was effective in two-thirds of the property.
C) One-third, because the bequest was one-third.
D) None, because the increase belongs to the estate.

Key Takeaway
Increase in value is apportioned according to ownership at the time of its occurrence; the buyer's share is the same as his ownership share of the original property.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

Decrease in Value and the Rule Against Annulment (Dawr)
Ruling when value decreases; explanation of prohibition on annulment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the beneficiary's compensation when the property decreases in value, and explain the prohibition on annulment due to circular reasoning.

Core Idea
The beneficiary cannot annul the sale to recover from the buyer; compensation is from the heirs, and annulment leads to infinite regress.

If the bequeathed property decreases after the heir's sale, the beneficiary is entitled to compensation from the heirs to make up the value of his bequest. However, he cannot simply annul the sale and recover his share from the buyer, because that would create a logical circularity (dawr) and potentially endless claims. This lesson explains the calculation and the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Determine the loss and who bears it
When the value decreases, the loss is shared proportionally between the buyer and the estate (beneficiary's share). The buyer's share (2/3) loses value, and the estate's share (1/3) loses value. The beneficiary's right is to one-third of the estate at the time of death? Actually, the bequest is of one-third of the slave-girl. If the value drops, the beneficiary is entitled to the shortfall from the heirs because the heir (who sold) is considered to have consumed the property (استهلكها الوارث بالبيع).
The heir is the one who sold and thereby disposed of the property; he is liable for the value at the time of sale.
2
Calculate the beneficiary's claim against the heirs
The beneficiary is entitled to one-third of the estate's value at the time of sale (since that is when the heir consumed it). The estate's value at sale included the two-thirds that were sold (value 200) plus the unsold one-third (value 100) = 300? Actually careful: The estate initially includes the whole slave-girl (300). The bequest is one-third of the slave-girl (100). After the sale, the estate's remaining assets are the unsold one-third (100) plus the claim against the heir? The passage gives a calculation: if the slave-girl decreases to 100, the beneficiary takes the slave-girl's remaining value (1/3 of 100 = 33.33) and claims the rest (100 - 33.33 = 66.67) from the heirs. Actually the text says: 'أخذ الموصى له ثلثها ويرجع على الورثة من قيمتها بأربعة وأربعين وأربعة أتساع درهم' which is 44.44. This seems different. It's complex; better to keep the steps clear: first compute what the beneficiary gets from the current slave-girl (1/3 of current value), then compute the deficit from his original bequest (1/3 of original value? Or 1/3 of estate at time of sale?), and claim from heirs.
The exact calculation requires careful reading; the step is to identify the principle: the beneficiary is compensated by the heirs up to the value of his bequest at the time of the heir's consumption.
3
Explain why annulment is impossible
The text argues that if the beneficiary could annul the sale of the remaining portion (the part that decreased), it would lead to circular reasoning (dawr) and infinite regress. Because annulling one part would require reassessing the bequest's right, which would necessitate further annulments, ad infinitum. Therefore, the right to annul is dropped entirely, and the beneficiary only has a claim against the heirs.
This is a classic example of sadd al-dhara'i' and blocking means that lead to infinity.

Why can the beneficiary not annul the sale to recover his share from the buyer when the property value decreases?
A) Because the sale is entirely valid and cannot be undone.
B) Because annulment would lead to circular reasoning and infinite regress.
C) Because the beneficiary lost his right when he did not ratify immediately.
D) Because the buyer is innocent and must be protected.

Key Takeaway
When bequeathed property decreases after a partial sale, the beneficiary cannot annul the sale; he must seek compensation from the heirs, and annulment is barred due to circular reasoning.
