Ruling on Bequest of Specific Animals and Trees and Their Produce
Explaining the rules for bequests of specific animals, trees, and their offspring or fruit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether after-acquired produce (offspring, fruit, milk, wool) of a bequeathed specific animal or tree is included in the bequest, distinguishing between specified and unspecified wording.

Core Idea
If the testator specifies the class (e.g., 'from my flock'), after-death accretions are included; if indefinite, they are not.

A bequest of a specific item raises the question: does it include what the item later produces? The answer depends on the testator's wording and the timing of the accretion. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi rules using the example of a sheep, a date palm, and two slave-girls. By the end, you will be able to apply these distinctions to any bequest of a specific animal or tree.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of bequest
Determine whether the testator used indefinite wording (e.g., 'a sheep') or specific wording (e.g., 'a sheep from my flock'). This is the primary factor.
Indefinite: no connection to a specific group. Specific: connected to a particular flock, garden, etc.
2
Determine the timing of the accretion
Check whether the offspring, fruit, or other produce arose before or after the testator's death. Accretions after death are potentially included; those before death are not.
The bequest takes effect at death, so pre-death accretions are not owed.
3
Apply the inclusion rule for specific bequests
If the testator said 'from my flock' (or similar), the bequest includes after-death accretions (offspring, milk, wool) that are still extant. Consumed amounts are not compensated.
Extant means the property still exists in kind.
4
Apply the rule for bequest of one of two
If the testator said 'one of these two', the heirs choose which to give. If they choose the one that gave birth after death, the child follows. But if the child was born before death, it does not follow.
The choice is the heirs', not the beneficiary's.
5
Handle loss of the bequeathed item
If all the specified animals perish except one, the beneficiary gets that one. If none remain, the heirs must pay from the estate.
This applies when the bequest is of a specific group, e.g., 'from my flock'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رجل أوصى لرجل بشاة من غنمه وقد لحقت الأولاد بالإمهات بعد موته فللورثة أن يعطوه شاة بدون ولدها، وإن قال شاة من غنمي سلموا معها ولدها وما حلب من لبنها وجزء من صوفها إن كان قائماً وما كان مستهلكاً من ذلك فلا يضمونه ونه لأن الوصية تناولت شاة من قطيع معين فتدخل زوائدها تحت الوصية ولذلك لو أوصى بنخلة ولم يقل من نخلي هذه يعطونه نخلة دون ثمرتها وإن قال من نخلي هذه وقد أثمرت بعد موته تبعها الثمر . هذا إذا أوصى بمعين، فلو أوصى بأحدهما قال فيه أيضاً ولو أوصى بإحدى هاتين الأمتين فولدت إحداهما أعطاه الورثة أيتهما شاؤوا، فلو أعطوا التي ولدت تبعها ولدها، ولو قال قد أوصيت بجارية من جواري هؤلاء أو قال بشاة من غنمي هذه فولدت في حياة الموصي فأراد الورثة بعد موته أن يعطوه من الأولاد لم يكن لهم ذلك، وإن أعطوه جارية أو شاة أو نخلة تبعها ثمرها ولا يتبعها أولادها وثمرتها الحادثة قبل موت الموصي لأنه إنما وجب له ذلك بالوصية بعد الموت وبعد الموت الإيجاب لا يتناول الزوائد الحادثة قبل الموت، فإن هلكت الأمهات إلا واحدة بعد موت الموصي كان حقه في هذه الواحدة وإن لم يبق شيء من الأمهات دفعوا إليه الأموال
A man bequeathed to another man a sheep from his flock, and the offspring have attached to their mothers after his death. The heirs may give him a sheep without its offspring. But if he said 'a sheep from my flock', they hand over with it its offspring and whatever milk was milked from it and part of its wool if it is still extant, but whatever of that has been consumed they do not guarantee, because the bequest encompassed a sheep from a specific flock, so its accretions enter under the bequest. For that reason, if he bequeathed a date palm and did not say 'from these date palms of mine', they give him a date palm without its fruit. But if he said 'from these date palms of mine' and it bore fruit after his death, its fruit follows it. This is if he bequeathed a specific item. But if he bequeathed one of two, he also said: If he bequeathed one of these two slave-girls, and one of them gave birth, the heirs give him whichever they wish. So if they give the one that gave birth, her child follows her. And if he said 'I have bequeathed a slave-girl from these slave-girls of mine' or said 'a sheep from this flock of mine' and it gave birth during the life of the testator, then the heirs after his death wish to give him from the offspring, they do not have that. But if they give him a slave-girl, a sheep, or a date palm, its fruit follows it, but its offspring and fruit that arose before the death of the testator do not follow it, because that became obligatory for him by the bequest after death, and after death the obligation does not encompass accretions that arose before death. So if the mothers perished except one after the death of the testator, his right is in this one; and if nothing of the mothers remains, they pay him from the funds.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage discusses bequests of specific animals or trees. The key distinction is whether the testator says 'a sheep' (indefinite) or 'a sheep from my flock' (specific). If indefinite, the heirs can give a sheep without its offspring. If specific, all after-acquired produce (offspring, milk, wool, fruit) is included if still extant; consumed amounts are not compensated. The same applies to a date palm: if specified 'from these palms', fruit after death follows; otherwise not. The second part deals with bequests of one of two items. If the testator says 'one of these two slave-girls', the heirs choose, and if they choose the one that gave birth after death, the child is included. However, if the offspring was born before death, it is not included because the bequest takes effect after death and does not cover pre-existing accretions. If all the specified animals perish except one, the beneficiary takes that one; if none remain, he is compensated from the estate.

Key Terms
الوصية بمعين (al-wasiyyah bi-mu'ayyan): A bequest of a specific, identifiable item (like a particular sheep or date palm).
زوائد (zawa'id): Accretions or increases on the bequeathed property, such as offspring, fruit, milk, wool, etc.
الورثة (al-warathah): The heirs who are obligated to execute the bequest from the estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A testator says: 'I bequeath a sheep from my flock.' After his death, the sheep gives birth. What must the heirs give?
A) The sheep without its offspring
B) The sheep with its offspring
C) Only the offspring
D) The value of the sheep

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the inclusion of after-death produce in a bequest of a specific animal or tree depends on whether the testator specified the class (e.g., 'from my flock') or used indefinite wording.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
Bequest to a Son Who Becomes an Heir Before Death
Ruling on bequest to a son who becomes an heir before death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a bequest to a son who becomes an heir before death is void, and explain the principle that the validity of a bequest is determined at the time of death.

Core Idea
A bequest is judged at death: if the beneficiary becomes an heir before then, the bequest becomes void.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq illustrates a key application of the rule 'no bequest to an heir' (لا وصية لوارث). When a father in terminal illness bequeaths to a non-Muslim son who later converts, or to a slave son who is freed before the father's death, the bequest becomes void because at the time of death the son is now an heir. The same principle applies to gifts and acknowledgments made during terminal illness, as they are also considered with reference to the time of death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial scenario
A father in marad al-mawt makes a bequest to his non-Muslim son or his slave son.
2
Recognize the change of status before death
The son converts to Islam or is emancipated before the father dies.
3
Understand the legal consequence
The bequest becomes void (batil).
4
Grasp the underlying principle
The validity of a bequest is determined at the time of death (i'tibar halat al-mawt). Since the son becomes an heir before death, the bequest is to an heir and thus invalid.
The hadith 'لا وصية لوارث' (No bequest to an heir) is the basis.
5
Extend to gifts and acknowledgments
The same ruling applies to gifts (hibah) and acknowledgments (iqrar) made during terminal illness, as they are also treated like bequests and judged at death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( ولابنه الكافر أو الرقيق في مرضه فاسلم الابن أو أعتق قبل موت الأب ثم مات بطل كالهبة وإقراره أي إذا أوصى لابنه الكافر أو لابنه الرقيق في مرضه فأسلم الابن أو عتق قبل موت الأب ثم مات من ذلك المرض بطلت الوصية له كما تبطل الهبة له والإقرار له بالدين، أما الوصية فلأن المعتبر فيها حالة الموت وهو وارث فيها فلا تجوز له والهبة حكمها مثل الوصية لما عرف في موضعه، وأما الإقرار فإن كان الابن كافراً فلا إشكال فيه لأن الإقرار وقع لنفسه وهو وارث بسبب كان ثابتاً عند الإقرار وهو البنوة فيمتنع لما فيه من تهمة إيثار البعض فكان كالوصية فصار كما إذا كان له ابن وأقر لأخيه في مرضه ثم مات الابن قبل أبيه وورثه أخوه المقر له، فإن كان الإقرار له يكون باطلاً لما ذكرنا؛ كذا في هذا بخلاف ما إذا أقر لامرأة في مرضه ثم تزوجها حيث لا يبطل الإقرار لها لأنها صارت وارثة بسبب حادث والإقرار يلزمه بنفسه وهي أجنبية حال صدوره فيلزم لعدم المانع من ذلك ويعتبر من جميع المال بخلاف الوصية لها لأنها ايجاب عند الموت وهي وارثة فلهذا اتحد الحكم فيهما في الوصية وافترقا في الإقرار حتى كانت الزوجة قائمة عند الإقرار وهي غير وارثة فإن كانت نصرانية أو أمة ثم أسلمت قبل موته أو أعتقت الإقرار لها لقيام السبب حال صدوره. وإن كان الابن عبداً فإن كان عليه دين لا يصح إقراره له لأن الإقرار وقع له وهو وارث عند الموت فتبطل كالوصية، وإن لم يكن عليه دين صح الإقرار لأنه وقع للمولى إذا العبد لا يملك وقيل الهبة له جائزة لأنها تمليك في لا يملك فيقع للمولى وهو أجنبي فيجوز بخلاف الوصية لأنها إيجاب عند الموت وهو وهو وارث عنده فيمتنع. وفي عامة الروايات هي في المرض كالوصية فيها لأنها وإن كانت منجزة صورة فهي كالمضاف إلى ما بعد الموت حكماً لأن حكمها يتقرر عند الموت ألا ترى أنها تبطل بالدين المستغرق ولا تجوز بما زاد على الثلث والمكاتب كالحر لأن الإقرار والهبة يقع له وهو وارث عند الموت فلا يجوز كالوصية كذا ذكر الشارح . قال رحمه الله : (والمقعد والمفلوج والأشل والمسلول إن تطاول ذلك ولم يخف منه الموت فهبته من كل المال لأنه إذا يصح الحال
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And regarding his non-Muslim or slave son during his illness, if the son becomes Muslim or is emancipated before the death of the father, then dies, the bequest becomes void, like the gift and his acknowledgment.' That is, if he bequeaths to his non-Muslim son or his slave son during his illness, then the son becomes Muslim or is emancipated before the death of the father, then the father dies from that illness, the bequest to him becomes void, just as the gift to him becomes void and the acknowledgment of debt to him becomes void. As for the bequest, because the consideration is the time of death, and he is an heir at that time, so it is not permissible for him. And the gift has the same ruling as the bequest, as known in its place. As for the acknowledgment, if the son is non-Muslim, there is no problem, because the acknowledgment occurred for himself and he is an heir due to a cause that was established at the time of acknowledgment, i.e., sonship, so it is prevented because of the suspicion of favoring some, so it is like the bequest. So it becomes as if he had a son and acknowledged a debt to his brother during his illness, then the son died before the father, and his brother (the acknowledged) inherited him, then the acknowledgment for him would be invalid due to what we mentioned. Similarly here. This is unlike if he acknowledged a debt to a woman during his illness then married her, where the acknowledgment for her does not become void, because she became an heir due to a new cause, and the acknowledgment is binding upon itself, and she was a stranger at the time of its issuance, so it is binding due to the absence of an impediment, and it is considered from all the wealth, unlike the bequest to her, because it is an obligation at death and she is an heir, so the two rulings are unified in the bequest and differ in the acknowledgment. Even if the wife was present at the time of acknowledgment and she was not an heir, if she was a Christian or a slave-girl then became Muslim before his death or was emancipated, the acknowledgment for her is valid due to the existence of the cause at the time of its issuance. And if the son is a slave, if there is debt on him, the acknowledgment for him is not valid, because the acknowledgment occurred for him and he is an heir at death, so it is void like the bequest. And if there is no debt on him, the acknowledgment is valid, because it occurred for the master, since the slave does not own property. It is said that the gift to him is permissible, because it is a transfer of ownership to one who does not own, so it falls to the master, who is a stranger, so it is permissible, unlike the bequest, because it is an obligation at death and he is an heir at that time, so it is prevented. And in most narrations, the gift during illness is like the bequest in it, because although it is executed in form, it is like added to after death in terms of ruling, because its ruling is settled at death. Do you not see that it becomes void due to overwhelming debt and is not permissible for more than one-third? And the mukatab is like a free man, because the acknowledgment and gift occur for him and he is an heir at death, so it is not permissible like the bequest. Thus mentioned the commentator. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And the quadriplegic, the paralyzed, the one with a withered hand, and the consumptive, if that continues and death is not feared from it, then his gift is from all his wealth, because then it is valid.'
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage discusses rulings on bequests, gifts, and acknowledgments made during terminal illness (marad al-mawt) to a son who is non-Muslim or a slave. If the son becomes Muslim or is emancipated before the father's death, and then the father dies, the bequest becomes void because at the time of death the son has become an heir, and a bequest to a legal heir is invalid without the consent of other heirs. The same applies to gifts and acknowledgments of debt, because they are also seen as having effect at death. The passage distinguishes between a bequest and an acknowledgment: if the beneficiary becomes an heir after the acknowledgment (like a woman who is later married), the acknowledgment remains valid because it was binding when she was a stranger. However, for a son, the cause of heirship (sonship) existed at the time of acknowledgment, so it is tainted by suspicion of partiality. The discussion also covers a slave son: if he has debts, the acknowledgment is void; if he has no debts, the acknowledgment is valid because it goes to his master. Similarly, gifts to a slave son are permissible because the slave does not own, so the gift goes to the master, who is a non-heir. However, a bequest to a slave son is void because at death he is an heir. Finally, the passage notes that for a chronically ill person whose condition is prolonged and death is not imminent, gifts are treated from all wealth (not limited to one-third), because such illness is not considered marad al-mawt.

Key Terms
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): Terminal illness; a disease that likely leads to death, during which gifts and bequests are subject to special restrictions (one-third rule, no bequest to heir).
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment of a debt or right; in this context, a debtor's acknowledgment during terminal illness.
هبة (hibah): Gift; a transfer of ownership without compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man in terminal illness bequeaths to his non-Muslim son. The son converts to Islam after the bequest but before the father dies. According to Hanafi law, the bequest is:
A) Valid, because the bequest was made when the son was not an heir
B) Void, because the son becomes an heir at death
C) Valid only if the father dies before the son converts
D) Void only if the son was a slave

Key Takeaway
A bequest (or gift/acknowledgment) made during terminal illness becomes void if the beneficiary becomes an heir before death, because the ruling depends on the time of death.

Distinguishing Cases: Acknowledgment and Gifts to a Later Heir
Distinctions in the validity of acknowledgments and gifts during terminal illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between cases where an acknowledgment or gift during terminal illness remains valid or becomes void, specifically in the context of a woman later married and a slave son.

Core Idea
An acknowledgment to a stranger remains valid even if she later becomes an heir, but an acknowledgment to a child is void because the cause of heirship existed.

This lesson delves into the refinements of the rule discussed earlier. The passage contrasts the case of a son (who was always a potential heir) with that of a woman who becomes an heir by marriage after the acknowledgment. It also addresses the special situation of a slave son and the difference between bequest, gift, and acknowledgment.

Guided Path
1
Understand why a son's acknowledgment is void
For a son, the cause of heirship (sonship) existed at the time of the acknowledgment, so there is suspicion of partiality.
This is contrasted with a woman who is a stranger at the time of acknowledgment.
2
Contrast with a woman married after acknowledgment
If a man acknowledges a debt to a woman during illness and then marries her, the acknowledgment is valid because she was a stranger when it was made.
The marriage is a new cause of heirship, not present originally.
3
Analyze the slave son scenario
If the slave son has debts, the acknowledgment is void; if no debts, it goes to the master and is valid.
4
Distinguish gift to slave son
A gift to a slave son goes to the master (who is a stranger) and is permissible, but a bequest is void because the slave son is an heir at death.
5
Include the mukatab
The mukatab (slave with a contract of manumission) is treated like a free man; acknowledgment and gift to him are void because he is an heir at death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( ولابنه الكافر أو الرقيق في مرضه فاسلم الابن أو أعتق قبل موت الأب ثم مات بطل كالهبة وإقراره أي إذا أوصى لابنه الكافر أو لابنه الرقيق في مرضه فأسلم الابن أو عتق قبل موت الأب ثم مات من ذلك المرض بطلت الوصية له كما تبطل الهبة له والإقرار له بالدين، أما الوصية فلأن المعتبر فيها حالة الموت وهو وارث فيها فلا تجوز له والهبة حكمها مثل الوصية لما عرف في موضعه، وأما الإقرار فإن كان الابن كافراً فلا إشكال فيه لأن الإقرار وقع لنفسه وهو وارث بسبب كان ثابتاً عند الإقرار وهو البنوة فيمتنع لما فيه من تهمة إيثار البعض فكان كالوصية فصار كما إذا كان له ابن وأقر لأخيه في مرضه ثم مات الابن قبل أبيه وورثه أخوه المقر له، فإن كان الإقرار له يكون باطلاً لما ذكرنا؛ كذا في هذا بخلاف ما إذا أقر لامرأة في مرضه ثم تزوجها حيث لا يبطل الإقرار لها لأنها صارت وارثة بسبب حادث والإقرار يلزمه بنفسه وهي أجنبية حال صدوره فيلزم لعدم المانع من ذلك ويعتبر من جميع المال بخلاف الوصية لها لأنها ايجاب عند الموت وهي وارثة فلهذا اتحد الحكم فيهما في الوصية وافترقا في الإقرار حتى كانت الزوجة قائمة عند الإقرار وهي غير وارثة فإن كانت نصرانية أو أمة ثم أسلمت قبل موته أو أعتقت الإقرار لها لقيام السبب حال صدوره. وإن كان الابن عبداً فإن كان عليه دين لا يصح إقراره له لأن الإقرار وقع له وهو وارث عند الموت فتبطل كالوصية، وإن لم يكن عليه دين صح الإقرار لأنه وقع للمولى إذا العبد لا يملك وقيل الهبة له جائزة لأنها تمليك في لا يملك فيقع للمولى وهو أجنبي فيجوز بخلاف الوصية لأنها إيجاب عند الموت وهو وهو وارث عنده فيمتنع. وفي عامة الروايات هي في المرض كالوصية فيها لأنها وإن كانت منجزة صورة فهي كالمضاف إلى ما بعد الموت حكماً لأن حكمها يتقرر عند الموت ألا ترى أنها تبطل بالدين المستغرق ولا تجوز بما زاد على الثلث والمكاتب كالحر لأن الإقرار والهبة يقع له وهو وارث عند الموت فلا يجوز كالوصية كذا ذكر الشارح . قال رحمه الله : (والمقعد والمفلوج والأشل والمسلول إن تطاول ذلك ولم يخف منه الموت فهبته من كل المال لأنه إذا يصح الحال
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And regarding his non-Muslim or slave son during his illness, if the son becomes Muslim or is emancipated before the death of the father, then dies, the bequest becomes void, like the gift and his acknowledgment.' That is, if he bequeaths to his non-Muslim son or his slave son during his illness, then the son becomes Muslim or is emancipated before the death of the father, then the father dies from that illness, the bequest to him becomes void, just as the gift to him becomes void and the acknowledgment of debt to him becomes void. Commentary
This passage discusses rulings on bequests, gifts, and acknowledgments made during terminal illness (marad al-mawt) to a son who is non-Muslim or a slave. If the son becomes Muslim or is emancipated before the father's death, and then the father dies, the bequest becomes void because at the time of death the son has become an heir, and a bequest to a legal heir is invalid without the consent of other heirs. However, for a son, the cause of heirship (sonship) existed at the time of acknowledgment, so it is tainted by suspicion of partiality. The discussion also covers a slave son: if he has debts, the acknowledgment is void; if he has no debts, the acknowledgment is valid because it goes to his master. Key Terms
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): Terminal illness; a disease that likely leads to death, during which gifts and bequests are subject to special restrictions (one-third rule, no bequest to heir).
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment of a debt or right; in this context, a debtor's acknowledgment during terminal illness.
هبة (hibah): Gift; a transfer of ownership without compensation.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has made a contract of manumission with his master, agreeing to pay a sum for his freedom.

Checkpoint

Chronic Illness and the Scope of Marad al-Mawt
Exception to marad al-mawt for chronic non-terminal conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the criteria for marad al-mawt and state that a chronic, non-terminal illness does not trigger restrictions on gifts and bequests.

Core Idea
If the illness is prolonged and death is not feared, the person is not in marad al-mawt; his gifts are valid from all wealth.

The final part of the passage clarifies a boundary condition. Not all illnesses invoke the strict rules of marad al-mawt. Conditions like quadriplegia, paralysis, withered hand, or consumption, if long-standing and not feared to lead to imminent death, are not considered terminal. Therefore, the person's gifts are treated as from all his wealth, not limited to one-third.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the conditions mentioned
The passage lists: al-muq'ad (quadriplegic), al-mafluj (paralyzed), al-ashal (one with a withered hand), al-maslul (consumptive).
2
Understand the qualifier
These conditions are prolonged (tatawala) and death is not feared (lam yukhaf minhu al-mawt).
3
Consequence
The gift from such a person is valid from all his wealth (hibatuhu min kull al-mal).
No one-third restriction.
4
Reason
Such a condition is not marad al-mawt, so the restrictions of terminal illness do not apply.
Gifts are treated as ordinary gifts, not deathbed dispositions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( ولابنه الكافر أو الرقيق في مرضه فاسلم الابن أو أعتق قبل موت الأب ثم مات بطل كالهبة وإقراره أي إذا أوصى لابنه الكافر أو لابنه الرقيق في مرضه فأسلم الابن أو عتق قبل موت الأب ثم مات من ذلك المرض بطلت الوصية له كما تبطل الهبة له والإقرار له بالدين، أما الوصية فلأن المعتبر فيها حالة الموت وهو وارث فيها فلا تجوز له والهبة حكمها مثل الوصية لما عرف في موضعه، وأما الإقرار فإن كان الابن كافراً فلا إشكال فيه لأن الإقرار وقع لنفسه وهو وارث بسبب كان ثابتاً عند الإقرار وهو البنوة فيمتنع لما فيه من تهمة إيثار البعض فكان كالوصية فصار كما إذا كان له ابن وأقر لأخيه في مرضه ثم مات الابن قبل أبيه وورثه أخوه المقر له، فإن كان الإقرار له يكون باطلاً لما ذكرنا؛ كذا في هذا بخلاف ما إذا أقر لامرأة في مرضه ثم تزوجها حيث لا يبطل الإقرار لها لأنها صارت وارثة بسبب حادث والإقرار يلزمه بنفسه وهي أجنبية حال صدوره فيلزم لعدم المانع من ذلك ويعتبر من جميع المال بخلاف الوصية لها لأنها ايجاب عند الموت وهي وارثة فلهذا اتحد الحكم فيهما في الوصية وافترقا في الإقرار حتى كانت الزوجة قائمة عند الإقرار وهي غير وارثة فإن كانت نصرانية أو أمة ثم أسلمت قبل موته أو أعتقت الإقرار لها لقيام السبب حال صدوره. وإن كان الابن عبداً فإن كان عليه دين لا يصح إقراره له لأن الإقرار وقع له وهو وارث عند الموت فتبطل كالوصية، وإن لم يكن عليه دين صح الإقرار لأنه وقع للمولى إذا العبد لا يملك وقيل الهبة له جائزة لأنها تمليك في لا يملك فيقع للمولى وهو أجنبي فيجوز بخلاف الوصية لأنها إيجاب عند الموت وهو وهو وارث عنده فيمتنع. وفي عامة الروايات هي في المرض كالوصية فيها لأنها وإن كانت منجزة صورة فهي كالمضاف إلى ما بعد الموت حكماً لأن حكمها يتقرر عند الموت ألا ترى أنها تبطل بالدين المستغرق ولا تجوز بما زاد على الثلث والمكاتب كالحر لأن الإقرار والهبة يقع له وهو وارث عند الموت فلا يجوز كالوصية كذا ذكر الشارح . قال رحمه الله : (والمقعد والمفلوج والأشل والمسلول إن تطاول ذلك ولم يخف منه الموت فهبته من كل المال لأنه إذا يصح الحال
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And regarding his non-Muslim or slave son during his illness, if the son becomes Muslim or is emancipated before the death of the father, then dies, the bequest becomes void, like the gift and his acknowledgment.' That is, if he bequeaths to his non-Muslim son or his slave son during his illness, then the son becomes Muslim or is emancipated before the death of the father, then the father dies from that illness, the bequest to him becomes void, just as the gift to him becomes void and the acknowledgment of debt to him becomes void. As for the bequest, because the consideration is the time of death, and he is an heir at that time, so it is not permissible for him. And the gift has the same ruling as the bequest, as known in its place. As for the acknowledgment, if the son is non-Muslim, there is no problem, because the acknowledgment occurred for himself and he is an heir due to a cause that was established at the time of acknowledgment, i.e., sonship, so it is prevented because of the suspicion of favoring some, so it is like the bequest. So it becomes as if he had a son and acknowledged a debt to his brother during his illness, then the son died before the father, and his brother (the acknowledged) inherited him, then the acknowledgment for him would be invalid due to what we mentioned. Similarly here. This is unlike if he acknowledged a debt to a woman during his illness then married her, where the acknowledgment for her does not become void, because she became an heir due to a new cause, and the acknowledgment is binding upon itself, and she was a stranger at the time of its issuance, so it is binding due to the absence of an impediment, and it is considered from all the wealth, unlike the bequest to her, because it is an obligation at death and she is an heir, so the two rulings are unified in the bequest and differ in the acknowledgment. Even if the wife was present at the time of acknowledgment and she was not an heir, if she was a Christian or a slave-girl then became Muslim before his death or was emancipated, the acknowledgment for her is valid due to the existence of the cause at the time of its issuance. And if the son is a slave, if there is debt on him, the acknowledgment for him is not valid, because the acknowledgment occurred for him and he is an heir at death, so it is void like the bequest. And if there is no debt on him, the acknowledgment is valid, because it occurred for the master, since the slave does not own property. It is said that the gift to him is permissible, because it is a transfer of ownership to one who does not own, so it falls to the master, who is a stranger, so it is permissible, unlike the bequest, because it is an obligation at death and he is an heir at that time, so it is prevented. And in most narrations, the gift during illness is like the bequest in it, because although it is executed in form, it is like added to after death in terms of ruling, because its ruling is settled at death. Do you not see that it becomes void due to overwhelming debt and is not permissible for more than one-third? And the mukatab is like a free man, because the acknowledgment and gift occur for him and he is an heir at death, so it is not permissible like the bequest. Thus mentioned the commentator. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And the quadriplegic, the paralyzed, the one with a withered hand, and the consumptive, if that continues and death is not feared from it, then his gift is from all his wealth, because then it is valid.'
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage discusses rulings on bequests, gifts, and acknowledgments made during terminal illness (marad al-mawt) to a son who is non-Muslim or a slave. If the son becomes Muslim or is emancipated before the father's death, and then the father dies, the bequest becomes void because at the time of death the son has become an heir, and a bequest to a legal heir is invalid without the consent of other heirs. The same applies to gifts and acknowledgments of debt, because they are also seen as having effect at death. The passage distinguishes between a bequest and an acknowledgment: if the beneficiary becomes an heir after the acknowledgment (like a woman who is later married), the acknowledgment remains valid because it was binding when she was a stranger. However, for a son, the cause of heirship (sonship) existed at the time of acknowledgment, so it is tainted by suspicion of partiality. The discussion also covers a slave son: if he has debts, the acknowledgment is void; if he has no debts, the acknowledgment is valid because it goes to his master. Similarly, gifts to a slave son are permissible because the slave does not own, so the gift goes to the master, who is a non-heir. However, a bequest to a slave son is void because at death he is an heir. Finally, the passage notes that for a chronically ill person whose condition is prolonged and death is not imminent, gifts are treated from all wealth (not limited to one-third), because such illness is not considered marad al-mawt.

Key Terms
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): Terminal illness; a disease that likely leads to death, during which gifts and bequests are subject to special restrictions (one-third rule, no bequest to heir).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The gift is void because he cannot give away all his wealth.
B) The gift is valid only up to one-third.
C) The gift is valid from all his wealth.
D) The gift is void because he is not in full health.

Key Takeaway
A chronic, non-terminal illness does not constitute marad al-mawt, so gifts and bequests from such a person are not limited to one-third.

Ruling on Bequest of Specified vs Unspecified Items and Offspring
Explains rulings on bequest of specific or unspecified items and the inclusion of offspring or produce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on bequest of a specific item versus an unspecified item from a group, and identify whether offspring or fruit born before the testator's death are included.

Core Idea
A bequest takes effect at death; pre-death offspring do not automatically follow the bequeathed mother.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a key distinction in Hanafi law of bequest: if a testator bequeaths a specific item, it is straightforward. But if he bequeaths one of two unspecified items, the heirs have a choice, and the timing of offspring matters. Understanding these rules is essential for drafting valid wills and resolving disputes over bequests.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of bequest
Determine if the bequest is specific (mu'ayyan) or unspecified (one of two, or from a group). The ruling differs based on this distinction.
2
Trace the heirs' choice
For an unspecified bequest, the heirs choose which item to give. If they give the mother that gave birth before death, her child follows; otherwise, the child is not included.
3
Apply the principle of time
The bequest vests at death. Offspring or fruit born before death are accretions that the bequest does not cover, because the obligation arises only at death.
This is the core ratio: the bequest is created at death, so it cannot include items that came into existence before that moment.
4
Determine the consequence if items perish
If all mothers perish except one, the legatee takes that one. If none remain, the legatee receives the value.
The value substitutes the bequest when the subject matter is lost after death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا إذا أوصى بمعين، فلو أوصى بأحدهما قال فيه أيضاً ولو أوصى بإحدى هاتين الأمتين فولدت إحداهما أعطاه الورثة أيتهما شاؤوا، فلو أعطوا التي ولدت تبعها ولدها، ولو قال قد أوصيت بجارية من جواري هؤلاء أو قال بشاة من غنمي هذه فولدت في حياة الموصي فأراد الورثة بعد موته أن يعطوه من الأولاد لم يكن لهم ذلك، وإن أعطوه جارية أو شاة أو نخلة تبعها ثمرها ولا يتبعها أولادها وثمرتها الحادثة قبل موت الموصي لأنه إنما وجب له ذلك بالوصية بعد الموت وبعد الموت الإيجاب لا يتناول الزوائد الحادثة قبل الموت، فإن هلكت الأمهات إلا واحدة بعد موت الموصي كان حقه في هذه الواحدة وإن لم يبق شيء من الأمهات دفعوا إليه الأموال
This is if he bequeathed a specific item. If he bequeathed one of two, he also said: if he bequeathed one of these two slave-girls, and one of them gave birth, the heirs give whichever they wish. If they give the one that gave birth, her child follows her. And if he said 'I have bequeathed a slave-girl from among these slave-girls of mine' or 'a sheep from among these sheep of mine', and she gave birth during the testator's lifetime, then the heirs after his death want to give him from the offspring, they do not have that right. But if they give him a slave-girl, or a sheep, or a palm tree, its fruit follows it, but its offspring and fruit that came into existence before the testator's death do not follow it, because that is only obligated to him by bequest after death, and after death the obligation does not encompass the accretions that occurred before death. If the mothers perished except one after the testator's death, his right is in that one. And if nothing of the mothers remains, they pay him the value.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage addresses rulings related to bequest of a specific versus an unspecified item from a group. The author begins by stating a previous ruling: if the testator bequeaths a specific item, certain rules apply. Then he discusses cases where the bequest is of one of two slave-girls or an unspecified sheep or slave-girl. The key principle is that offspring or fruit born before the testator's death do not automatically belong to the legatee unless the heirs choose to give them. The reason is that the bequest takes effect at death, and the testator's will cannot include items that came into existence before death. If the mothers perish except one, the legatee takes that one; if all perish, he receives the value. This is a clarification from the Hanafi school on the scope of a bequest.

Key Terms
وصية بمعين (wasiyya bi-mu'ayyan): A bequest of a specific, identified item.
وصية بأحدهما (wasiyya bi-ahadihima): A bequest of one of two unspecified items, chosen by the heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Wasiyyah — Bequest

Bequest, Gift, and Acknowledgment to Heir Who Becomes Muslim or Free
Compares rulings of bequest, gift, and acknowledgment to a son who becomes Muslim or free before the father's death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the rulings on bequest, gift, and acknowledgment made during deathbed illness to a son who is a disbeliever or slave, and apply the condition of heirship at death to determine validity.

Core Idea
A deathbed bequest, gift, or acknowledgment to a son who later becomes an heir is void — timing of heirship determines validity.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines three legal instruments—bequest, gift, and acknowledgment of debt—made during a deathbed illness to a son who is either a disbeliever or a slave. The key question is whether the son's conversion to Islam or emancipation before the father's death affects the validity of these dispositions. The Hanafi school provides nuanced rules based on the timing of heirship, distinguishing between existing and newly acquired heir status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three legal acts and the son's initial status
The passage covers wasiyya (bequest), hiba (gift), and iqrar (acknowledgment) made during marad al-mawt (deathbed illness) to a son who is either a disbeliever or a slave.
The son's status (disbeliever/slave) means he is not initially an heir, but he may become an heir later.
2
Apply the principle that a bequest to an heir is invalid
A bequest to an heir is void. If the son becomes Muslim or free before the father's death, he becomes an heir at the moment of death, so the bequest is void.
The same applies to a gift made in illness, which is treated like a bequest.
3
Analyze the timing of heirship for acknowledgment (iqrar)
For iqrar, the key is whether the son was already an heir at the time of the acknowledgment. If the cause of heirship (sonship) existed at that time, the iqrar is void. If he becomes an heir by a new cause (e.g., conversion after the iqrar), the iqrar stands.
This differs from bequest/gift because iqrar is binding at its time, while bequest takes effect at death.
4
Examine the special case of the slave son
If the son is a slave, iqrar may fall to the master (if the slave has no debt), and then the master is a non-heir, so the iqrar can be valid. A gift to a slave son is also said to be permissible because it falls to the master. However, the majority view treats gifts in illness like bequests.
The mukatab (slave in contract of manumission) is like a free person in these rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( ولابنه الكافر أو الرقيق في مرضه فاسلم الابن أو أعتق قبل موت الأب ثم مات بطل كالهبة وإقراره أي إذا أوصى لابنه الكافر أو لابنه الرقيق في مرضه فأسلم الابن أو عتق قبل موت الأب ثم مات من ذلك المرض بطلت الوصية له كما تبطل الهبة له والإقرار له بالدين، أما الوصية فلأن المعتبر فيها حالة الموت وهو وارث فيها فلا تجوز له والهبة حكمها مثل الوصية لما عرف في موضعه، وأما الإقرار فإن كان الابن كافراً فلا إشكال فيه لأن الإقرار وقع لنفسه وهو وارث بسبب كان ثابتاً عند الإقرار وهو البنوة فيمتنع لما فيه من تهمة إيثار البعض فكان كالوصية فصار كما إذا كان له ابن وأقر لأخيه في مرضه ثم مات الابن قبل أبيه وورثه أخوه المقر له، فإن كان الإقرار له يكون باطلاً لما ذكرنا؛ كذا في هذا بخلاف ما إذا أقر لامرأة في مرضه ثم تزوجها حيث لا يبطل الإقرار لها لأنها صارت وارثة بسبب حادث والإقرار يلزمه بنفسه وهي أجنبية حال صدوره فيلزم لعدم المانع من ذلك ويعتبر من جميع المال بخلاف الوصية لها لأنها ايجاب عند الموت وهي وارثة فلهذا اتحد الحكم فيهما في الوصية وافترقا في الإقرار حتى كانت الزوجة قائمة عند الإقرار وهي غير وارثة فإن كانت نصرانية أو أمة ثم أسلمت قبل موته أو أعتقت فلا يصح الإقرار لها لقيام السبب حال صدوره. وإن كان الابن عبداً فإن كان عليه دين لا يصح إقراره له لأن الإقرار وقع له وهو وارث عند الموت فتبطل كالوصية، وإن لم يكن عليه دين صح الإقرار لأنه وقع للمولى إذا العبد لا يملك وقيل الهبة له جائزة لأنها تمليك في لا يملك فيقع للمولى وهو أجنبي فيجوز بخلاف الوصية لأنها إيجاب عند الموت وهو وارث عنده فيمتنع. وفي عامة الروايات هي في المرض كالوصية فيه لأنها وإن كانت منجزة صورة فهي كالمضاف إلى ما بعد الموت حكماً لأن حكمها يتقرر عند الموت ألا ترى أنها تبطل بالدين المستغرق ولا تجوز بما زاد على الثلث والمكاتب كالحر لأن الإقرار والهبة يقع له وهو وارث عند الموت فلا يجوز كالوصية كذا ذكر الشارح .
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And for his disbelieving son or slave son in his illness, if the son becomes Muslim or is freed before the father's death, then he dies, it becomes void like a gift and his acknowledgment). That is, if he bequeaths to his disbelieving son or his slave son in his illness, and the son becomes Muslim or is freed before the father's death, then he dies from that illness, the bequest to him is void, just as a gift to him is void and an acknowledgment of debt to him is void. As for the bequest, because the consideration is the state of death, and he is an heir at that time, so it is not permissible for him. The gift has the same ruling as the bequest as is known in its place. As for the acknowledgment: if the son was a disbeliever, there is no problem with it because the acknowledgment occurred for himself and he is an heir due to a cause that was established at the time of the acknowledgment, which is sonship, so it is prevented because of the suspicion of favouring some, so it is like a bequest. So it becomes like the case where a man has a son and acknowledges a debt to his brother in his illness, then the son dies before the father, and the acknowledged brother inherits him; then the acknowledgment to him is invalid for what we have mentioned. Likewise in this. Contrary to the case where he acknowledges for a woman in his illness and then marries her: the acknowledgment does not become void because she became an heir due to a new cause, and the acknowledgment is binding on him itself, and she was a non-heir at the time of its occurrence, so it is binding due to the absence of an impediment, and it is considered from all the property, unlike a bequest to her because it is an obligation at death and she is an heir, so for this reason the ruling for both is the same in bequest and they differ in acknowledgment, until the wife was a non-heir at the time of acknowledgment. If she was a Christian or a slave-girl and then became Muslim or was freed before his death, the acknowledgment to her is not valid because the cause existed at the time of its occurrence. And if the son was a slave: if he had a debt, his acknowledgment to him is not valid because the acknowledgment occurred for him and he is an heir at death, so it becomes void like a bequest. If he had no debt, the acknowledgment is valid because it falls to the master, since the slave does not own. And it is said that a gift to him is permissible because it is a transfer of ownership from one who does not own, so it falls to the master who is a non-heir, so it is permissible, unlike a bequest because it is an obligation at death and he is an heir, so it is prevented. In most narrations, the gift in illness is like a bequest because, although it is immediate in form, it is like that which is deferred to after death in effect, because its ruling is determined at death. Do you not see that it is voided by overwhelming debt and is not valid for more than a third? And the mukatab is like a free person because the acknowledgment and gift fall to him and he is an heir at death, so it is not permissible like a bequest. Thus mentioned the commentator.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This is a detailed intra-Hanafi and comparative discussion on the rulings of bequest, gift, and acknowledgment of debt made during a deathbed illness to a son who is either a disbeliever or a slave. The author explains that if the bequest is made to such a son and he later becomes Muslim or is freed before the father's death, the bequest becomes void because at the time of death the son becomes an heir, and a bequest to an heir is invalid. The same applies to a gift (hiba) made in illness, as it is treated like a bequest. However, for an acknowledgment of debt (iqrar), there is a distinction: if the son is a disbeliever at the time of acknowledgment, it is invalid because he is an heir by cause (sonship) at that moment. But if the son later becomes an heir by a new cause (e.g., conversion) after the acknowledgment, the acknowledgment stands. The text also contrasts the case of acknowledging a debt to a woman who later marries the testator: the acknowledgment is valid because she was not an heir at the time. For a slave son, the acknowledgment may be valid if he has no debt, because it falls to the master (who is a non-heir). A gift to a slave son is also permissible for similar reasons. The overarching principle is that gifts made in illness are generally treated like bequests, limited to one-third and subject to debts, except where the recipient is a non-heir at the time. This passage reflects Hanafi fiqh's careful consideration of the timing of heirship and the intent to circumvent inheritance laws.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment of a debt or right; a unilateral declaration.
هبة في المرض (hiba fi al-marad): A gift made during a deathbed illness.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of manumission with his master, with payments scheduled.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The acknowledgment is valid because it was made before conversion.
B) The acknowledgment is void because the son was an heir by cause at the time of acknowledgment.
C) The acknowledgment is valid for up to one-third of the estate.
D) The acknowledgment becomes void only if the father recovers.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of bequests, gifts, and acknowledgments made during deathbed illness depends critically on whether the recipient becomes an heir before the testator's death and whether that heirship existed at the time of the act.

Chronic vs Acute Illness: Gifts from All Wealth or One-Third
Distinguishes chronic from acute illness for gift validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between chronic stable illness and acute death-sickness (marad al-mawt) in Hanafi law and state the effect on the validity of gifts from the entire wealth.

Core Idea
A chronic stable illness does not restrict gifts; only acute death-sickness imposes the one-third limit.

This lesson examines a crucial Hanafi rule: not all severe illnesses are considered marad al-mawt. Gifts made by a quadriplegic, paralyzed, or consumptive person may be fully valid from all wealth if the condition is long-standing and stable. But if the illness worsens and death is feared, gifts are limited to one-third. Understanding this distinction is essential for advising clients and drafting wills.

Guided Path
1
Name the four chronic conditions
Identify the four conditions mentioned: maq'ad (quadriplegic), maflooj (paralyzed), ashal (withered hand), maslool (consumptive). These are examples of conditions that may be chronic or acute.
The ruling is not limited to these; it applies analogically.
2
Separate the two scenarios
If the condition has become chronic (tatawul) and death is not feared, gifts are from all wealth. The commentator equates this to blindness or lameness—stable states that do not prevent full capacity.
Key phrase: 'if that has been long-standing and death is not feared from it'.
3
Identify the acute scenario
If the condition is not long-standing, or if it worsens and death is feared, it is marad al-mawt. Gifts are then restricted to one-third. Even if a stable condition later worsens to bedriddenness, it is treated as acute.
The commentator: 'if he becomes bedridden after long-standing, it is like a new illness'.
4
Apply the principle
Given a donor's condition at the time of the gift, determine if it is stable/chronic or acute/progressive. Check fear of death and progression.
Focus on the state at the moment of gifting, not the underlying chronic label.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (والمقعد والمفلوج والأشل والمسلول إن تطاول ذلك ولم يخف منه الموت فهبته من كل المال وإلا فمن الثلث . ثم قال الشارح: تقادم العهد صار من طبعه كالعمى والعرج، وهذا لأن المانع من التصرف مرض الموت ومرض الموت لا يكون سبباً للموت غالباً وإنما يكون سبباً للموت إذا كان بحيث يزداد حالاً فحالاً إلى أن يكون آخره الموت وأما إذا استحكم وصار بحيث لا يزداد ولا يخاف منه الموت لا يكون سبباً آخره الموت كالعمى ونحوه ولهذا لا يستقل بالتداوي. قال رحمه الله: (وإلا فمن الثلث) أي إن لم يتطاول يعتبر تصرفه من الثلث إذا كان صاحب فراش ومات منه في أيامه لأنه من ابتدائه يخاف منه الموت ولهذا يتداوى فيكون من مرض الموت، وإن صار صاحب فراش بعد التطاول فهو كمرض حادث به حتى تعتبر تبرعاته من الثلث؛ كذا ذكر الشارح والله تعالى أعلم.
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And the quadriplegic, the paralyzed, the one with a withered hand, and the consumptive: if that has been long-standing and death is not feared from it, then his gift is from all of his wealth; otherwise, it is from one-third.) Then the commentator said: If the condition has become chronic and become part of his nature like blindness and lameness. This is because the impediment to transactions is death-sickness, and death-sickness is not generally a cause of death; rather, it is a cause of death only if it is such that it worsens condition by condition until its end is death. But if it becomes stable and such that it does not worsen and death is not feared from it, it is not a cause whose end is death, like blindness and the like, and for this reason he does not need to treat himself. He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (Otherwise, it is from one-third.) That is, if it is not long-standing, his transaction is considered from one-third if he is bedridden and dies from it within its days, because from the beginning death is feared from it, and therefore he treats himself, so it is death-sickness. And if he becomes bedridden after long-standing, it is like a new illness in him, so his donations are considered from one-third. Thus mentioned the commentator, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal status of gifts made by individuals suffering from chronic conditions: the quadriplegic (maq'ad), the paralyzed (maflooj), the one with a withered hand (ashall), and the consumptive (maslool). The ruling distinguishes between two scenarios: if the condition has been long-standing and there is no fear of death from it (i.e., it is stable and not progressive), then the gift is valid from the entirety of one's wealth, just like a healthy person. This is because the impediment of marad al-mawt (death-sickness) does not apply; such chronic conditions are akin to blindness or lameness. However, if the condition is acute (not long-standing), such that it worsens and death is feared, then it is considered marad al-mawt, and gifts are restricted to one-third of the estate, as with any deathbed transaction. The commentator adds that if the condition becomes long-standing but later the person becomes bedridden, it is treated as a new acute illness, and the one-third restriction applies from that point. This ruling is important for determining whether a terminally ill person's donations are subject to the limits of wasiyya.

Key Terms
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): A terminal or deathbed illness from which death is feared.
تطاول (tatāwul): Long-standing or chronic condition that becomes habitual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man has been paralyzed for many years and is not expected to die from it. He gives a gift of his entire house. What is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The gift is valid from his entire wealth.
B) The gift is only valid from one-third.
C) The gift is void.
D) The gift is valid only if heirs consent.

Key Takeaway
Chronic stable illness does not trigger marad al-mawt restrictions; only acute progressive illness with fear of death limits gifts to one-third.

Freeing Slaves in Illness: Bequest and Sa'y Calculation
Chapter introduction: freeing in illness as bequest and sa'y calculation example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how a slave's sa'y is calculated when he is freed during the master's deathbed illness and has paid part of his value.

Core Idea
Freeing a slave in death-sickness is a bequest from the one-third; sa'y is recalculated based on the estate at distribution.

This passage introduces the crucial Hanafi ruling that freeing a slave during marad al-mawt (death-sickness) is legally treated as a bequest (wasiyya) from the one-third of the estate. The author presents a detailed example from al-Mabsut to illustrate how sa'y (the slave's work to pay off the value) is recalculated when the slave has made a partial payment during the master's lifetime, emphasizing that the estate is considered on the day of distribution, not the day of the bequest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is freeing a slave during the master's death-sickness. The ruling is that it is treated as a bequest (wasiyya) from the one-third of the estate. If the slave's value falls within the one-third, no sa'y is required; otherwise, sa'y is needed for the excess.
This applies only when the freeing occurs in marad al-mawt, not in health.
2
Understand the condition of the bequest
The bequest of freeing is limited to one-third of the estate. If the slave's value exceeds one-third, the excess portion is not a bequest and becomes an obligation on the slave through sa'y.
The one-third is calculated from the net estate after funeral expenses and debts.
3
Recognize the concept of sa'y
Sa'y is the slave's obligation to work to pay off the value owed to the master's estate. Although it becomes due after the master's death, the cause (sabab) is the act of freeing. Hastening the payment during the master's life is valid because the cause already exists.
Hastening payment is like hastening zakat before the year ends but after the cause exists.
4
Work through the example
Consider a slave valued at 300 dirhams. He hastens to pay 200 dirhams during the master's life, and the master spends it. The master dies with no other property. The estate on the day of distribution is 100 dirhams. The bequest of freedom is one-third of 100 = 33.33 dirhams. Since the slave already paid 200, he receives 33.33 as his bequest share, but must perform sa'y for two-thirds of the remaining 100 dirhams, i.e., 66.67 dirhams.
The slave is free immediately upon payment of 200, but sa'y remains for the balance.
5
Apply the principle of day of distribution
The estate is calculated on the day of distribution, not the day of the bequest. Because the master spent the 200 dirhams during his life, that amount is not part of the estate. Only the remaining 100 is considered. This principle affects the calculation of sa'y and the bequest share.
This prevents the slave from being overburdened by a larger estate that no longer exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب العتق في المرض والوصية بالعتق لما كان الإعتاق في المرض من أنواع الوصية وكان له أحكام مخصوصة أفرده بباب على حدة وأخرجه عن صريح الوصية لأن الصريح هو الأصل. قال رحمه الله : (تحريره في مرضه) يعني يكون وصية فإن خرج من الثلث لا سعاية عليه وسيأتي حكم ذلك إن شاء الله تعالى . أطلق في كونه وصية فشمل ما إذا عجل البدل أو بعضه فمات السيد أو مات العبد قبل السيد وترك مالاً وما إذا أعتق على مال أو لا. قال في المبسوط: مسائله تشتمل على فصول : إحداها في تعجيل المعتق السعاية إلى مولاه والثاني في ترك السعاية بعد موته، والثالث في تعجيل بعض السعاية في حياته وترك السعاية بعد موته. وإذا أعتق عبداً في مرضه قيمته ثلاثمائة فعجل العبد لمولاه مائتي درهم فأنفقها ثم مات ولا مال له غيرها يسعى في ثلثي المائة الباقية وسلم له ثلث المائة وهو حر لأن العتق في مرض الموت وصية في الوصايا يعتبر مال الميت يوم القسمة لا يوم الوصية ومال الميت : يوم القسمة مائة درهم لأنه لما عجل ثلثي السعاية في حياة المولى صح التعجيل لأنه عجل بعد وجود سبب الوجوب لأن السعاية تجب عليه بعد الموت لكن بالسبب السابق وهو العتق وتعجيل الحكم بعد وجود سبب الوجوب جائزة كتعجيل الزكاة وغيرها فصار المعجل ملكاً للمولى وقد أنفقها في حياته في حاجته والوصايا تنفذ عما يفضل عن حاجته الحالية، والفاضل عن مائة درهم وقد أوصى للعبد بجميع المائة فيكون له ثلث المائة الباقية، ولو عجل قيمته كلها فأنفقها لم يسع في شيء لأنه أدى قيمة نفسه مرة بعد ما صار مكاتباً عند أبي حنيفة، وحراً
Chapter on freeing slaves in illness and bequest of freeing. Since freeing in illness is a type of bequest and has specific rulings, he isolated it in a separate chapter and removed it from explicit bequest because the explicit is the original. He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (His freeing in his illness) meaning it is a bequest. If it comes from the one-third, there is no sa'y upon him, and the ruling for that will come, Allah willing. He made it general that it is a bequest, so it includes whether he hastened the substitute or part of it and the master died, or the slave died before the master leaving property, and whether he freed for a consideration or not. He said in al-Mabsut: Its issues comprise chapters: one on the freed slave hastening the sa'y to his master, the second on leaving sa'y after his death, and the third on hastening part of the sa'y during his lifetime and leaving sa'y after his death. If a man frees a slave in his illness whose value is three hundred, and the slave hastens to give his master two hundred dirhams, and he spends them, then the master dies with no property other than that, the slave works for two-thirds of the remaining hundred, and one-third of the hundred is given to him, and he is free. Because freeing in death-sickness is a bequest among bequests; the deceased's wealth is considered on the day of distribution, not the day of the bequest. The deceased's wealth on the day of distribution is one hundred dirhams. Because when he hastened two-thirds of the sa'y during the master's lifetime, the hastening was valid because it occurred after the existence of the cause of obligation. The sa'y becomes obligatory upon him after death, but by a prior cause, i.e., the freeing. Hastening the ruling after the existence of the cause of obligation is permissible, like hastening zakat and other things. So the hastened amount becomes the master's property, and he spent it during his life for his needs. Bequests are executed from what remains after his immediate needs. The remainder is one hundred dirhams, and he bequeathed to the slave all of it, so he gets one-third of the remaining hundred. And if he hastened all of his value and he spent it, he does not work for anything because he paid his value once after he became a mukatab according to Abu Hanifa, and he is free.

Commentary
This is the opening of the chapter on freeing slaves during deathbed illness. The author (Ibn Nujaym) explains that such freeing is legally treated as a bequest (wasiyya) from the one-third of the estate. He then discusses the concept of sa'y (the slave working to pay off the value to the master). The chapter covers three scenarios: (1) the slave hastens to pay the entire sa'y while the master is alive, (2) he leaves sa'y after the master's death, and (3) he hastens part and leaves part. A detailed example is given: a slave valued at 300 dirhams is freed in the master's illness. The slave gives 200 dirhams during the master's life, and the master spends it. Later the master dies with no other property. On the day of distribution, the estate is only 100 dirhams. The bequest to the slave is for his freedom, and since it is a bequest, it is limited to one-third of the estate. However, the slave has already paid 200, which is more than the value, but because the master spent it, the slave owes sa'y for the remaining value? Actually, the calculation: The estate is 100 dirhams. The bequest of freedom is for the slave's full value (300), but only one-third (100) is effective. However, the slave already paid 200, so his freedom is valid; he must work for the remaining 100? Wait, the text says 'يسعى في ثلثي المائة الباقية' meaning he works for two-thirds of the remaining hundred? That seems inconsistent. Let me re-read: The slave hastened 200, master spent it, then master dies with no other property. The estate is 100 (the 200 is gone). The bequest is for the slave's freedom, and the effective bequest is one-third of the 100 = 33.33? But the text says 'يسعى في ثلثي المائة الباقية وسلم له ثلث المائة' meaning he works for two-thirds of the remaining 100 and is given one-third of the 100. Actually, I think the reasoning: The slave's value is 300, he paid 200, so his obligation (sa'y) is 100. But the bequest from the estate is one-third of the estate (100), which goes to the slave. However, the slave already paid 200, so the net: he owes 100 sa'y, and he receives 33.33 as bequest? That would not make sense. Perhaps the example means: The estate is 100 (the 200 spent is gone). The bequest of freedom is considered from the estate. The slave is entitled to one-third of the estate (33.33) as a bequest, but he still owes sa'y for the remaining value? The text says 'يسعى في ثلثي المائة الباقية' which is 66.66, and 'سلم له ثلث المائة' i.e., 33.33. So the slave gets 33.33 as his bequest share, but he must work for 66.66 as sa'y, so net he works for 33.33? This is a complex calculation. The commentary should stick to explaining what the text says without adding independent rulings. The passage is a detailed example from al-Mabsut. The main point is that freeing in illness is a bequest, and the slave's payments and sa'y are adjusted according to the estate at the day of distribution.

Key Terms
سعاية (sa'y): The slave's work to pay off the value to the master.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has contracted to purchase his freedom.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Marital Gift Calculation During Illness
Intra-Hanafi calculation methods for a marital gift during illness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the different calculation methods of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad for a marital gift during illness, and state the common final result.

Core Idea
Three Hanafi imams agree on the wife's bequest amount but differ in calculating the revolving share.

In cases where a husband gifts property to his wife during terminal illness, and she predeceases him, the calculation of the wife's bequest and the husband's estate involves a unique challenge: the 'revolving share' (السهم الدائر). This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the methods of the three founding Hanafi imams—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—who all arrive at the same final bequest of thirty dirhams but take different mathematical paths. Understanding their approaches deepens your appreciation of Hanafi inheritance jurisprudence and the precision required in bequest calculations.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Scenario
Identify the key facts: a husband gives his wife a gift with favoritism (محاباة) during illness. She dies before him. The gift is treated as a bequest (وصية) and must not exceed one-third of the estate. The husband later also dies. The calculation involves integrating the wife's inheritance from the husband and the bequest.
The gift value is fifty dirhams; the wife's dower (mahr) is also fifty. The husband's total estate is eighty dirhams.
2
Grasp the Revolving Share (السهم الدائر)
The revolving share is a portion of the estate that appears to belong to one heir but then returns to the other due to inheritance, requiring subtraction to avoid double-counting. This concept is central to the dispute.
It arises because the wife inherits from the husband, but her bequest also comes from his estate, creating a circular calculation.
3
Follow Abu Hanifa's Method
Abu Hanifa first returns the deficiency (twenty dirhams) to the husband's estate, then adds the wife's dower, finds half for the husband, and adjusts. His method avoids the revolving share by treating the gift as a direct deduction.
Result: husband gets sixty, wife's bequest thirty, satisfying the one-third limit.
4
Follow Abu Yusuf's Method
Abu Yusuf calculates the wife's share of the favoritism (one-third of fifty = sixteen and two-thirds), adds dower, takes half for the husband, then identifies the revolving share and subtracts it from the husband's portion. He uses multiplication to resolve fractions.
His method explicitly handles the revolving share by dividing the inherited portion into three shares and iterating.
5
Follow Muhammad's Method
Muhammad starts similarly but divides the estate into two shares (husband gets half, wife gets half by inheritance). He then applies the bequest to the husband's share and adjusts using multiplication. His method is more direct.
He also arrives at a wife's bequest of thirty, but through a different allocation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويرد عشرون على ورثة الزوج نقصاً للوصية بالمحاباة، ثم يضم ثلاثون إلى مهر مثلها وذلك خمسون فصار ثمانين للزوج نصفه وذلك أربعون وينقص أربعون ثم ما أصاب الزوج من أربعين يضم إلى ما أخذه بنقص الوصية وذلك عشرون فصار له ستون وقد نفذنا الوصية في ثلاثين فاستقام الثلث والثلثان وأما تخريج أبي يوسف أن مال الزوج لما حابى به وذلك خمسون فيكون لها ثلث المحاباة وذلك ستة وعشر وثلثان ولا يعتبر ماله بما يرث لما بينا في الباب المتقدم، ثم يضم ستة عشر وثلثين إلى مهر مثلها وذلك خمسون فيصير ستة وستين وثلثين للزوج نصف ذلك بالميراث وذلك ثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث فهذا مال استفاده الزوج بالميراث فيجعل على ثلاثة أسهم سهم للمرأة فيعود نصفه إلى الزوج بالميراث فانكسر فأضعف صار ستة للمرأة سهمان فيعود منها سهم إلى الزوج فهذا هو السهم الدائر فاطرحه من نصيب الزوج يبقى له ثلاثة وللمرأة سهمان وذلك ثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث على خمسة خمساه للمرأة وذلك ثلاثة عشر وثلث درهم يضم ذلك إلى ستة عشر فصار ثلاثين. وأما تخريج محمد بأن للمرأة ثلث المحاباة وذلك ستة عشر وثلثان يضم ذلك إلى مهر مثلها وذلك خمسون فصار ستة وستين وثلثا درهم فيجعل ذلك على سهمين سهم للزوج فقد مات الزوج عن سهم للمرأة ثلث ذلك بالوصية فانكسر بالثلث فاضرب سهمين في ثلاثة فصار ستة للزوج ثلاثة وللمرأة سهم فصار المال ستة وهو وستون وثلثان على خمسة خمس ذلك للمرأة وذلك ثلاثة عشر وثلث يضم إلى ما أعطينا لها في الابتداء وذلك ستة عشر وثلثان فصار وصيتها ثلاثين.
Twenty is returned to the husband's heirs as a deficiency of the bequest due to favoritism. Then thirty is added to her dower, making fifty, so total becomes eighty. Half of that for the husband is forty, and forty is deficient. Then the husband's share of forty is added to what he took by deficiency of the bequest, which is twenty, so he has sixty. We have executed the bequest in thirty, so one-third and two-thirds are correct. As for the method of Abu Yusuf: the husband favored her by fifty, so she gets one-third of the favoritism, which is sixteen and two-thirds. He does not consider his wealth from inheritance as we explained in the previous chapter. Then sixteen and two-thirds is added to her dower, which is fifty, making sixty-six and two-thirds. The husband gets half of that by inheritance, which is thirty-three and one-third. This is wealth the husband acquired by inheritance, so it is divided into three shares: one share for the wife, then half of it returns to the husband by inheritance. It becomes broken, so multiply by two, making six. The wife has two shares, of which one returns to the husband, and this is the revolving share. Subtract it from the husband's share, leaving him three and the wife two. That amount, thirty-three and one-third, is divided into five parts. Two-fifths for the wife is thirteen and one-third dirhams, which is added to sixteen, making thirty. As for the method of Muhammad: the wife gets one-third of the favoritism, which is sixteen and two-thirds, added to her dower of fifty, making sixty-six and two-thirds dirhams. This is divided into two shares: one share for the husband. The husband died, so the wife gets one-third of that share by bequest, which is broken by the third. Multiply the two shares by three, making six: three for the husband, one for the wife. So the estate is six, which is sixty-six and two-thirds divided into five parts. One-fifth for the wife is thirteen and one-third, added to what we gave her initially, which is sixteen and two-thirds, making her bequest thirty.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage presents a specific case: a husband during terminal illness gives a gift to his wife with favoritism (محاباة). The wife dies before the husband. The issue is how to calculate the husband's estate and the wife's bequest. The three Hanafi imams agree on the final result (the wife's bequest is thirty) but differ in the method of calculation, particularly regarding the 'revolving share' (السهم الدائر). Abu Hanifa's method is presented first: he returns twenty to the husband's heirs as deficiency, adds thirty to the wife's dower, and so on. Abu Yusuf considers the husband's favoritism as fifty, gives the wife one-third of that as per bequest, and then adjusts for the inherited share, using multiplication to resolve the fractional issues. Muhammad's method starts similarly but divides the estate into two shares (since the wife predeceases, the husband inherits from her), then applies the bequest to the husband's share, and finally distributes. The passage illustrates the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf in solving such inheritance and bequest problems. The commentator emphasizes that the result is the same, but the path differs.

Key Terms
السهم الدائر (al-sahm al-da'ir): A share that appears in the estate but is effectively returned because it is inherited back; it must be subtracted to avoid double-counting.
محاباة (muhabat): Favoritism in a sale or gift, where the price is below market value. Here, the husband gives a gift worth more than the bequest limit.
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A bequest made during illness, limited to one-third of the estate unless heirs consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a husband giving a gift to his wife during illness with the wife predeceasing, how do Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad differ?
A) They differ on the final amount of the wife's bequest.
B) They differ on the method of calculation but agree on the final result.
C) They differ on whether the gift is valid.
D) They differ on the ruling of the gift being a bequest.

Key Takeaway
The three Hanafi imams agree that the wife's bequest is thirty dirhams, but they differ in their calculation methods, with Abu Hanifa's being the preferred approach.

Gift During Illness Treated as Will
Ruling that a gift during illness has the same legal effect as a will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a gift made during terminal illness and identify its limitations.

Core Idea
A gift during terminal illness is treated as a will, limited to one-third of the estate.

In Hanafi fiqh, a gift (hiba) given during a terminal illness (marad al-mawt) is not treated like an ordinary gift. The author of Kanz al-Daqa'i'q states a concise rule: 'His gift is a will.' This means it is subject to the rules of wasiyyah, including the one-third limit. The ruling applies regardless of whether the gift is revocable or not, and whether the recipient is an heir or a stranger.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a gift (hiba) made by a person during a terminal illness. According to the text, its ruling is that it is treated as a will (wasiyyah), not as a normal gift.
This is a classification ruling – the gift is legally equivalent to a bequest.
2
Understand the scope of the ruling
The ruling is general: it applies whether the gift returns to the donor or not, and whether the donee is an heir or a non-heir. No exceptions are mentioned.
This means the gift is always considered a will, regardless of these factors.
3
Apply the consequential limitations
Because it is treated as a will, the gift is limited to one-third of the donor's estate unless all heirs consent to more. This is the key practical outcome.
The one-third limit is a core rule of wasiyyah in Hanafi law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وهبته وصية) يعني حكمها حكم الوصية أي إذا وهب المريض في مرضه يكون حكمه حكم الوصية. أطلق في الهبة فشمل ما إذا عادت للمريض أو لم تعد وللأجنبي وللوارث .
The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'His gift is a will,' meaning its ruling is the ruling of a will. That is, if a sick person gives a gift during his illness, its ruling is the ruling of a will. He made it general in the gift, so it includes whether it returns to the sick person or not, and whether it is for a stranger or an heir.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage states a fundamental principle in Hanafi fiqh: any gift (hiba) made by a person during a terminal illness (marad al-mawt) is legally treated as a will (wasiyyah). This means it is only enforceable up to one-third of the estate unless the heirs consent to more. It applies regardless of whether the gift is revocable or not, and it applies to both heirs and non-heirs. This ruling is found in the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq and is being commented upon here.

Key Terms
وهبته وصية (hibatuhu wasiyyah): A gift made during a terminal illness is legally considered a will, limited to one-third of the estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It requires consent of all heirs regardless of amount.

Key Takeaway
A gift during terminal illness is governed by the law of wills, not ordinary gifts.
