Gift During Illness and Sale Back: Calculation
Ruling with calculation examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the net amount due from a donee when a gift by a sick person is sold back to the donor, applying the Hanafi rule that gifts during illness are treated as bequests from the one-third.

Core Idea
A gift during illness is a bequest; if the donee sells it back, the value is added to the estate, and the donee's share is capped at one-third of the adjusted net wealth.

This lesson unpacks two mathematical examples from al-Muntaqa. A sick person gifts a slave girl, the donee sells her back for cash, then the donor dies. The passage walks through the precise calculation of what the donee ultimately owes the donor's heirs. Understanding this calculation is essential for applying the rule that gifts during illness are bequests limited to one-third of the estate.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the gift as a bequest
Any gift by a person in his final illness (marad al-mawt) is treated as a bequest (wasiyyah) and thus can only be executed from up to one-third of the estate, without requiring the consent of other heirs.
This is the foundational Hanafi rule behind the calculation.
2
Treat the sale back as a valid sale by a healthy owner
When the donee sells the item back to the donor while healthy, it is as if the donee owned the item and sold it. The sale price becomes a debt owed by the donor to the donee.
The donee's ownership is recognized; the sale is not voided by the donor's illness.
3
Add the value of the gift to the donor's estate as a debt from the donee
Since the donee sold the item back, the item's value is considered as if it were still in the donor's estate, but now as a debt owed by the donee. This increases the donor's total assets.
The donor's estate is inflated by the value of the gifted item, then reduced by any debt the donor owed to the donee (the sale price).
4
Compute the net estate available for bequests
Subtract any debts of the donor from the total assets. The bequest portion is one-third of this net figure.
The donee's claim as a bequest is one-third of the net estate, not the original value of the gift.
5
Offset the donee's claim against his debt to the estate
The donee is entitled to receive the bequest amount, but he also owes the estate the value of the gift (because the item was sold back). After setting off the bequest, the remaining debt is what the donee must pay to the heirs.
In the first example, the donee's bequest of 166.67 is offset against his debt of 200? Actually the numbers: read carefully from the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال في المنتقى : وهب المريض لرجل أمة وقيمتها ثلاثمائة ولا مال له غيرها فباعها الموهوب له للواهب وهو صحيح بمائة درهم ولم يقبض المائة، ثم مات الواهب من مرضه والجارية تسلم لورثة الواهب ويأخذون من الموهوب له ثلاثة وثلاثين درهماً وثلثاً لأنه حين باعها إياه كان كأنه قد استملك الجارية وصارت قيمتها ديناً عليه وهي ثلثمائة فكانت هذه الثلاثمائة زيادة في مال الميت فصار ماله ستمائة إلا أن عليه دين مائة درهم فصار ماله الذي تجوز فيه وصيته خمسمائة درهم فللموهوب له ثلثها وذلك مائة وستة وستون وثلثان فيكون ذلك وصية قيمة الأمة يبقى عليه مائة وثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث وقد كان له على الواهب مائة ديناً يبقى عليه ثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث ولو وهب المريض أمة قيمتها ستمائة . فباعها الموهوب له من الواهب بمائتي درهم ثم ماتا جميعاً ولا مال لواحد منهما غيرها فإن الجارية تباع وتدفع المائتين إلى ورثته لأن الهبة قد نفذت من الثلث فينفذ بيعه من الواهب في الثلث لأن بيع المريض لا يجوز إلا بمثل قيمته وقيمته ثلثها مائة درهم فيرد ذلك القدر من ثمنها إلى تركة الموهوب له .
He said in al-Muntaqa: A sick person gave a slave girl to a man, valued at three hundred, and he had no other property. Then the donee sold her back to the donor while he was healthy for one hundred dirhams, but did not take possession of the hundred. Then the donor died from his illness, and the slave girl is surrendered to the donor's heirs. They take from the donee thirty-three and one-third dirhams. Because when the donee sold her to him, it was as if he had owned the slave girl, and her value became a debt against him, being three hundred. So this three hundred was an increase to the deceased's wealth, making his total six hundred, except that he owed a debt of one hundred dirhams, so his wealth that allows his bequest is five hundred dirhams. The donee is entitled to one-third of that, which is one hundred sixty-six and two-thirds, which is the bequest of the slave girl's value. There remains upon the donee one hundred thirty-three and one-third, and he had a debt of one hundred against the donor, so net he owes thirty-three and one-third. And if a sick person gave a slave girl worth six hundred, and the donee sold her back to the donor for two hundred dirhams, then both died, and neither had any other property, then the slave girl is sold and the two hundred are given to the donee's heirs because the gift was executed from the one-third. The sale from the donor is also executed from the one-third, because the sick person's sale is only valid for equivalent value, and its value is one-third of her, which is one hundred dirhams. So that amount from its price is returned to the donee's estate.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage from al-Muntaqa provides two examples illustrating the application of the rule that gifts during illness are treated as bequests. In the first scenario, a sick person gifts a slave girl worth 300 (his only asset). The donee sells her back to the donor when he is healthy for 100 but does not take payment. The donor then dies from his illness. The slave girl is kept by the donor's heirs, and the donee must pay 33.33 to the heirs. The calculation: the donee's sale back effectively makes the slave's value a debt due to the donor, increasing the donor's estate to 600, but he owes the donee 100, so net 500. One-third of that is 166.67, but the donee had already paid 100? Actually the text says the donee owes 133.33 net after offsetting the 100 debt. It's complex. The second example: If both donor and donee die, and the gift was for 600 with sale back for 200, the slave is sold and the 200 goes to the donee's heirs, but only 100 of the sale price is valid because the sick person's sale is limited to one-third of his estate, which is 100. So the remaining 100 stays with the donor's estate.

Key Terms
المنتقي (al-Muntaqa): A work by Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim al-Samarqandi, a Hanafi jurist, containing selected issues.
الموهوب له (al-mawhub lahu): The donee, the recipient of the gift.
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): Bequest; a disposition of property after death, limited to one-third of the estate without consent of heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first example from al-Muntaqa, why does the donee owe 33.33 dirhams to the donor's heirs?
A) Because the gift was invalid.
B) Because the donee's debt of 100 is offset by the bequest of 166.67, leaving a net of 33.33.
C) Because the donor's estate is only 300.
D) Because the donee did not pay the 100 for the sale.

Key Takeaway
Gifts during illness are treated as bequests; the donee's entitlement is limited to one-third of the net estate, and any subsequent sale back to the donor is effective but adjusted through a precise offset calculation.

Gift of a Slave with Debt and Manumission by Donee
Ruling on a sick person gifting a fully encumbered slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the validity of manumission by the donee of a gifted slave whose debt covers its value, distinguishing between manumission before and after the donor's death.

Core Idea
The donee's manumission is valid before death but invalid after because creditors' rights attach after death.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from the Hanafi fiqh of gifts (hibah) and manumission (itq) when the gifted property is fully encumbered by debt. The key nuance is the effect of time: the donee's ownership is secure only during the donor's lifetime; after death, the slave reverts to the estate for debt collection, nullifying the gift and any subsequent manumission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the legal issue
The case: a terminally ill person (mariḍ) gifts a slave whose debt (dayn muhīṭ) equals or exceeds its value, and the donor has no other property. The issue is whether the donee's manumission of the slave is valid, and when.
The debt 'encompasses' the value, meaning the slave is not net positive for the donor's estate.
2
Distinguish before and after the donor's death
The text gives two rulings: (1) if the donee manumits the slave before the donor dies, the manumission is valid because the donee owns the slave at that time. (2) If manumission occurs after the donor's death, it is invalid because the creditor's right has attached to the slave for sale and collection, and the slave is consumed by debt.
The difference hinges on the timing: before death, the gift is complete (presumably with delivery); after death, the gift is annulled and the slave reverts to the donor's estate.
3
Understand the underlying legal principle
The ruling is based on the principle that a debt consumes the property (dayn muhīṭ prevents the slave from being part of the free estate). Before death, the donee's ownership is effective; after death, creditors' rights supersede the gift, making it void ab initio. Therefore, the donee cannot manumit what he no longer owns.
This aligns with Hanafi rules on the priority of debt over bequests and gifts from a terminally ill person.
4
Apply the ruling to similar cases
Generalize: if a terminally ill person gives any property fully encumbered by debt, the donee's actions (like manumission) are valid only if performed during the donor's lifetime. After death, the gift fails and any action on the property is invalid.
The same principle applies to sales, bequests, and other transfers from a terminally ill person when debt exceeds assets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مريض وهب عبده الرجل وعليه دين محيط بقيمته ولا مال له غيرها فأعتقه الموهوب له قبل موت المريض جاز عتقه لأنه أعتق ما يملكه وإن أعتقه بعد موته لم يجز عتقه لأنه تعلق حق الغريم به بيعاً واستيفاء وصار مستغرقاً بدينه فانقضت الهبة من الأصل وعاد إلى قديم ملكه أعتق مالاً يملكه
A sick person gave away his slave to a man, and the slave had a debt encompassing its value, and the sick person had no other property. If the donee manumits him before the sick person's death, his manumission is valid because he manumitted what he owns. But if he manumits him after his death, his manumission is not valid because the right of the creditor has attached to the slave for sale and collection, and the slave becomes consumed by the debt. So the gift is annulled from its origin and returns to its former ownership. He manumitted property he owns? (incomplete).
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage deals with a specific scenario: a sick person gifts a slave who is already fully encumbered by debt (the debt equals or exceeds the slave's value), and the donor has no other property. Since the slave's value is consumed by the debt, the gift is not effective against creditors. If the donee (recipient) manumits the slave before the donor's death, the manumission is valid because at that moment the donee truly owns the slave (the gift having been completed by delivery perhaps?). But if the manumission occurs after the donor's death, the slave is considered part of the donor's estate subject to debt collection, so the gift fails and the slave returns to the donor's ownership. The final phrase 'أعتق مالاً يملكه' seems to be a repetition or note.

Key Terms
دين محيط (dayn muhit): A debt that covers the entire value of the slave, meaning the slave's value is entirely consumed by the debt.
هبة (hibah): Gift; transfer of ownership without compensation.
عتق (itq): Manumission; freeing a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Only after the donor's death.
C) Both before and after death.
D) Neither before nor after death.

Key Takeaway
The validity of the donee's manumission depends on timing: it is valid before the donor's death but invalid after, because creditors' rights nullify the gift posthumously.

Acknowledgment of Paternity by a Sick Person: The Condition of the Master's Confirmation
Ruling on a sick person acknowledging a slave as his son.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a sick person's acknowledgment of a slave as his son leads to inheritance, and apply the rule to distinguish between confirmation during life and after death.

Core Idea
A sick person's acknowledgment of paternity only establishes lineage and inheritance if the slave's master confirms it during the sick person's lifetime.

In Hanafi law, a terminally ill person may declare that a slave owned by someone else is actually his son. This lesson examines the critical factor that determines whether such an acknowledgment leads to inheritance: the timing of the master's confirmation. Based on the authoritative narration from Abu Yusuf, the ruling distinguishes between confirmation during the sick person's life, which makes the acknowledgment effective, and confirmation after death, which renders it void.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the scenario
The case involves a sick person who states that a slave belonging to another man is his son. Note that the slave is owned by a third party, not by the declarant.
The slave's ownership matters because acknowledgment of paternity alone cannot override the master's rights.
2
Identify the crucial condition
The key condition is the master's affirmation (tasdiq) of the claim. Abu Yusuf states that inheritance only occurs if the master confirms during the sick person's lifetime.
If the master denies or is silent, the acknowledgment has no effect.
3
Understand the timing rule
If the master confirms after the sick person's death, the acknowledgment is considered void. The reason is that the declarant's death ends the possibility of a valid iqrar (acknowledgment).
Iqrar is a legal act that cannot survive the death of the declarant.
4
Apply to the manumission scenario
The same rule applies when the sick person acknowledges that the master has already manumitted his son (who is a slave). Inheritance occurs only if the master confirms during his lifetime.
The principle is consistent: confirmation must be contemporaneous with the declarant's life.
5
Conclude with the practical outcome
Thus, for inheritance to pass, two conditions must be satisfied: (1) the sick person's acknowledgment, and (2) the master's confirmation before the sick person dies.
This ruling prevents disputes after death where evidence may be unreliable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال محمد مريض أقر لعبد رجل أنه ابنه ثم مات قال أبو يوسف : إن صدقه السيد في حياة المريض ورثه لأنه ثبت نسبه منه بتصادقهما، فإن صدقه بعد موته لا يرثه لأن إقراره قد بطل بموته. وذكر الحسن بن زياد عن أبي يوسف في مريض له ابن معروف وهو عبد لرجل فأقر المريض أن المولى قد أعتق ابنه قال إن صدقه في حياته ورثه إذا مات، وإن صدقه بعد موته لم يرثه لما بينا
Muhammad said: A sick person acknowledged that the slave of a man is his son, then he died. Abu Yusuf said: If the master affirms him during the sick person's lifetime, he inherits from him because his lineage is established by their mutual affirmation. But if he affirms after his death, he does not inherit because his acknowledgment has become void by his death. Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Yusuf concerning a sick person who has a known son who is a slave of a man: the sick person acknowledged that the master has manumitted his son. He said: If he affirms him during his lifetime, he inherits when he dies. But if he affirms after his death, he does not inherit for the reason we explained.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage discusses a case where a terminally ill person claims that a slave owned by another person is actually his son. If the master confirms this during the sick person's life, the lineage is established (by the mutual acknowledgment of the two free men), and the son inherits from the sick father. However, if the master only confirms after the sick person's death, the acknowledgment is considered void because the declarant is dead, and lineage cannot be established after death. The same applies to a case where the sick person acknowledges that his son (who is a slave of someone) was manumitted by that master: if the master confirms during life, the son is free and inherits; if after death, no inheritance.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment of a right or status; here specifically acknowledgment of paternity and manumission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the slave is not free.
B) Because the acknowledgment becomes void by the declarant's death.
C) Because the master's confirmation is always unreliable.
D) Because inheritance requires a written will.

Key Takeaway
A sick person's acknowledgment of a slave as his son only leads to inheritance if the master confirms the claim during the sick person's lifetime; confirmation after death is legally void.

The Revolving Share: Method of Subtraction in Spousal Bequests
Summary of intra-Hanafi methods for the revolving share.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani on the method of subtracting the revolving share (السهم الدائر) and state the preferred view.

Core Idea
Imams agree on final shares but differ in method: Abu Hanifa subtracts from total wealth, Muhammad from bequeathed wealth.

When both spouses make bequests to each other during terminal illness, a cycle (السهم الدائر) can occur if one dies first. The three Hanafi imams agree on the final distribution but use different methods to eliminate the double counting. This lesson unpacks their reasoning and the preferred approach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Understand the scenario: husband and wife each bequeath to the other during terminal illness. If one dies, a portion of the estate cycles back. The 'revolving share' must be subtracted to avoid counting twice.
2
State the points of agreement
Note that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad agree on the final shares; the difference is only in the method of calculation.
3
Contrast the two methods
Abu Hanifa subtracts the revolving share from the total estate (جملة المال). Muhammad subtracts it from the bequeathed portion (الموصى به). Trace each reasoning: Abu Hanifa sees the cycle as arising from inherited wealth; Muhammad sees it as arising from the bequest itself.
4
Analyze the tarjih (preference)
The text states al-Sahih is Abu Hanifa's view because the wife's bequest to the husband effectively comes from the husband's wealth (since she inherited from him). So the operation is from his side, making subtraction from his share more appropriate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو وهب أحد الزوجين لصاحبه في المرض أصله أن أجوبتهم لمسائل الباب متفقة وتخاريجهم لها مختلفة فأبو حنيفة اعتبر جميع الموصي في القسمة وطرح السهم الدائر من جملة المال لأن الدور يقع بسبب المال المستفاد بالميراث وأنه لو لم يرث منها شيئاً بأن كان عليها دين مستغرق لجميع ماله لم يقع الدور، ومحمد اعتبر القسمة في المال الموصى به وطرح السهم الدائر من المال المستفاد بالوصية لأن الدور يقع من ذلك فإنه لو لم يستفد شيئاً بالوصية بأن كان على الزوج دين مستغرق يقع الدور، والصحيح ما قاله أبو حنيفة لأن الوصية للمرأة والمرأة للزوج من وصيتها إنما توزع من مال الزوج لا من مالها فكان العمل من ماله فكان طرح السهم الدائر من نصيبه أولى.
And if one of the spouses gave a gift to the other during illness, its basis is that their answers to the issues of the chapter are agreed, but their methods of derivation are different. Abu Hanifa considered all of the testator's wealth in the division and subtracted the revolving share from the total wealth because the revolving occurs due to the wealth acquired by inheritance. And if she had not inherited anything from him, such as if she had a debt encompassing all his wealth, the revolving would not occur. Muhammad considered the division in the wealth that is bequeathed and subtracted the revolving share from the wealth acquired by the bequest because the revolving occurs from that. Because if he had not acquired anything by the bequest, such as if the husband had a debt encompassing all his wealth, the revolving would not occur. The correct view is what Abu Hanifa said because the bequest is for the woman, and the woman's share for the husband from her bequest is only distributed from the husband's wealth, not from her wealth. So the operation is from his wealth, so subtracting the revolving share from his portion is more appropriate.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage explains the underlying principles of the three Hanafi imams in dealing with the 'revolving share' in cases of gifts between spouses during terminal illness. The core issue is a double bequest: the husband bequeaths to the wife, and the wife bequeaths to the husband, but since one may predecease the other, a share can cycle. Abu Hanifa's principle: consider all the testator's wealth and subtract the revolving share from the total estate. Muhammad's principle: consider only the bequeathed wealth and subtract the revolving share from that. The commentator states that the correct view is Abu Hanifa's because the wife's bequest to the husband is actually paid from the husband's estate (since the wife's share of his bequest comes from his wealth), so the revolving share should be subtracted from the husband's portion.

Key Terms
السهم الدائر (al-sahm al-da'ir): A share in inheritance that is inherited back from the beneficiary, causing a cycle; it must be eliminated to avoid counting twice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, whose view on subtracting the revolving share is correct?
A) Muhammad's view.
B) Abu Hanifa's view.
C) Abu Yusuf's view.
D) The view of the two companions (Sahibayn).

Key Takeaway
The three Hanafi imams agree on final shares in mutual bequest cases, but Abu Hanifa's method of subtracting the revolving share from the total estate is the preferred view.

The Gift Between Spouses During Illness: Hybrid of Hiba and Wasiyya
Classification and first chapter: husband's gift to wife in illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three classifications of gifts between spouses during illness and explain why a gift from husband to wife is not voided if the wife predeceases the husband.

Core Idea
A gift during illness is a real gift for ownership and a will for the one-third limit.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq classifies gifts between spouses during illness into three chapters and begins the first chapter with a detailed case. The key legal issue is the dual nature of such gifts: they are treated as a real gift (hiba) for ownership and as a will (wasiyya) for the one-third limit. This hybrid status affects the consequences when the donee predeceases the donor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three classifications
The passage opens with three chapters: (1) husband's gift to wife during his illness, (2) husband's gift to wife plus bequest to a stranger, and (3) gift of each spouse to the other. Note the systematic division.
2
Parse the hypothetical case
A husband gifts his wife 100 dirhams during his illness with no other wealth. The wife dies before the husband, then the husband dies. The text explores the legal status of the gift.
The wife becomes a 'stranger' (ajnabiyya) in terms of inheritance because she predeceases the husband.
3
Understand the hybrid nature
The gift is a real gift (hiba) because ownership transfers immediately upon possession (qabd). It is also a will (wasiyya) because it is subject to the one-third limit. Therefore, the donee's death does not void the gift if possession occurred; the gift is valid and passes to her heirs.
Key Arabic phrase: 'والهبة لا تبطل بموت الموهوب له قبل موت الواهب بعد ما تمت بالقبض'
4
Examine the calculation
The text derives the distribution according to Abu Hanifa: the husband's estate (100) is divided such that the husband's heirs receive 80 and the wife's agnates receive 20. The complete calculation involves treating the gift as a will from one-third, then inheritance adjustments.
The passage ends while beginning Abu Yusuf's derivation, so the full steps are incomplete.
5
Note the legal principle
The principle: A gift completed by possession is not invalidated by the donee's prior death. This overrides the general rule that a will is void if the legatee dies before the testator.
The hybrid nature leads to a unique ruling: the gift survives the donee's death up to the one-third limit.

Source Text

ثم المسائل على فصول : أحدها في هبة الزوج لامرأته في مرضه، والثاني في هبته في مرضه لامرأته ووصيته لأجنبي، والثالث في هبة كل واحد من الزوجين لصاحبه. وإذا وهب لامرأته في مرضه مائة لا مال له غيرها وماتت ومات وتركت عصبة للزوج لورثة درهم الزوج ستون ببعض الهبة وجازت في أربعين للزوج من ذلك عشرة بميراثه ولعصبتها عشرون لأنها لما ماتت قبل موت الزوج صارت أجنبية ولم تبق وارثة قبل موت الزوج فصحت الهبة لها فلم تبطل الهبة لها، وإن كانت الهبة المنفذة وصية والوصية تبطل موت الموصى له قبل موت الموصي لأنها هبة حقيقية حتى ملكها الموهوب له في الحال وصية حكماً حتى الثلث والهبة لا تبطل بموت الموهوب له قبل موت الواهب بعد ما تمت بالقبض، وباعتبار وصية تنفذ من الثلث عملاً بالشبهين ولا يجوز إبطالها بالشك بعد صحتها. ثم تخريجه أن لأبي حنيفة وهو المائة الموهوبة فيجعل على ثلاثة أسهم لحاجتين لأجل المال للزوج جميع الوصية للمرأة وذلك سهم وسهمان للزوج ماتت المرأة عن سهم فيكون ميراث ميراثاً وعصبتها نصفين وقد انكسر بالنصف فأضعف فصار ستة فصار للزوج أربعة ولها سهمان فيعود إلى الزوج سهم بالميراث منها وهو السهم الدائر فاطرحه من نصيب الزوج فكان نصيبه أربعة فبقي له ثلاث ولها سهمان فصار جميع مال الزوج على خمسة خمسا المائة وذلك أربعون لها بالوصية وللزوح ثلاثة أخماسها ،ستون، ثم يعود إلى الزوج نصف حصتها بالميراث فصار للزوج ثمانون ولعصبتها عشرون وأما تخريج أبي يوسف وهو أن مال الزوج ما يرث منها لا أن بين زوجها
Then the issues are divided into chapters: one: the husband's gift to his wife during his illness; two: his gift to his wife and his bequest to a stranger; three: the gift of each spouse to the other. If he gives his wife one hundred during his illness, having no other wealth, and she dies and he dies, and she leaves agnates. The husband's heirs get sixty by some of the gift, and it is valid for forty. The husband gets ten of that by inheritance, and her agnates get twenty. Because when she died before the husband, she became a stranger and was no longer an heir before the husband's death, so the gift to her was valid, so the gift is not void for her. Although the executed gift is a will, and a will becomes void with the death of the legatee before the testator, but this is a real gift in that the donee immediately owns the item, and a will only regarding the one-third limit. A gift does not become void by the death of the donee before the donor after it has been completed by possession. Considering it as a will executed from one-third acting on both similarities, and it is not permissible to invalidate it due to doubt after its correctness. Then its derivation according to Abu Hanifa: the gifted one hundred is divided into three shares due to two needs: the husband gets all of the bequest for the wife? Actually more complex. The text continues with the calculation.

Commentary
This passage classifies the issues related to gifts between spouses during illness into three chapters. It then begins the first chapter: a husband gives his wife 100 dirhams when he has no other wealth. The wife dies before the husband. The gift is treated as a will limited to one-third. The calculation: the husband's estate is 100, one-third is 33.33? But the text says the husband's heirs get 60 and the wife's agnates get 20? Actually it says the husband gets 60 by some of the gift and it is valid for 40? The passage is complex. It explains that even though the gift is like a will, it is also a real gift because possession is taken, so it does not become void by the donee's death. Then it gives Abu Hanifa's calculation: the 100 is divided into three shares? Then it breaks into fractions, eventually resulting in the husband getting 80 and the wife's agnates 20. The last part cuts off.

Key Terms
فصل (fasl): A chapter or section classifying the different types of gifts between spouses during illness.
هبة (hiba): A gift that transfers ownership immediately upon offer, acceptance, and possession.
وصية (wasiyya): A bequest that takes effect after death, limited to one-third of the estate.
شبهان (shabahan): Two similarities: the gift resembles both a hiba and a wasiyya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the gift from husband to wife not become void when the wife predeceases the husband?
A) Because it is a real gift that has been completed by possession.
B) Because it is a will and wills are not voided by death.
C) Because the wife's agnates inherit it.
D) Because the husband did not die yet.

Key Takeaway
A gift during death illness is a hybrid: a real gift if possession taken, and a will for the one-third limit, so it survives the donee's prior death, with a complex inheritance calculation.

Manumission During Terminal Illness: Timing and Validity
Ruling on validity of manumission during illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on manumission by a terminally ill person and explain why emancipation after death is invalid due to the attachment of creditors' rights.

Core Idea
Manumission during illness is valid based on ownership; after death it is invalid due to creditors' rights.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a critical question: if a terminally ill person frees a slave, does the emancipation stand? The answer hinges on timing — emancipation during life is a valid exercise of ownership, but emancipation that takes effect after death conflicts with the rights of creditors, who have a prior claim on the estate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: (1) the sick person frees a slave during his illness, and (2) he frees the slave after his death (i.e., the emancipation is contingent on death).
2
State the ruling for each
In the first case, the manumission is valid (jā'iz); in the second, it is invalid (lā yajūz).
The passage explicitly states the outcome for both.
3
Analyze the reasoning for validity
During illness, the person owns the slave and can dispose of his property. The act of manumission is an exercise of ownership, so it is valid.
The text says 'because he freed what he owned' (li-annahu aʿtaqa mā yamlikuhu).
4
Analyze the reasoning for invalidity
After death, the slave becomes part of the estate, and creditors' rights attach to the estate. The emancipation would be a gift from the estate, which is invalid if it exceeds the one-third limit and prejudices creditors.
The text mentions 'the right of the creditor has attached to it by way of sale and recovery'.
5
Derive the legal principle
The key principle is that the validity of manumission depends on ownership at the time of the act and the absence of conflicting rights (creditors).
This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school; other schools may treat it as a bequest subject to the one-third rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موت المريض جاز عتقه لأنه أعتق ما يملكه وإن أعتقه بعد موته لم يجز عتقه لأنه تعلق حق الغريم به بيعاً واستيفاء وصار مستغرقاً بدينه فانقضت الهبة من الأصل وعاد إلى قديم ملكه أعتق مالاً يملكه
The death of the sick person: his manumission is valid because he freed what he owned. If he frees after his death, his manumission is not valid because the right of the creditor has attached to it by way of sale and recovery, and it became completely consumed by his debt, so the gift is annulled from the origin and returns to his former ownership. He freed property he owns.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: when a person who is terminally ill (marīḍ mawt) frees a slave during his illness, the manumission is valid because he owned the slave at the time of emancipation. However, if the emancipation is made contingent upon his death (i.e., it takes effect after death), it is not valid because the slave becomes part of the estate and is subject to creditors' rights. The slave's value is consumed by debt, so the emancipation is treated as a gift (hiba) from the estate, which is invalid as it exceeds the one-third limit if there are debts. The passage emphasizes that the ruling is based on ownership at the time of the act.

Key Terms
موت المريض (mawt al-marīḍ): The death of a person who was terminally ill (marīḍ mawt) – the time at which the validity of his dispositions is assessed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a terminally ill person's manumission of a slave become invalid according to this passage?
A) If he frees the slave during his illness
B) If he frees the slave after his death
C) If he frees the slave in the presence of a creditor
D) If the slave is worth more than one-third of his estate

Key Takeaway
The validity of manumission by a terminally ill person hinges on whether it is done during life (valid) or after death (invalid due to creditors' rights).

Acknowledgment of Lineage and Manumission During Illness
Ruling on acknowledgment by a sick person of a slave being his son or freed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for the validity of an acknowledgment of lineage or freeing made during terminal illness and apply it to determine inheritance.

Core Idea
An acknowledgment of paternity or freeing during illness requires confirmation during the declarant's life to effect inheritance.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents two rulings from Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on acknowledgments made during terminal illness. The key principle is that such acknowledgments are treated like bequests: they take effect only if accepted or confirmed during the declarant's lifetime. Understanding this condition prevents confusion about posthumous claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage covers two cases: (1) a sick person acknowledges a slave as his son, and (2) a sick person says his son has been freed by the master. Note that both involve third-party consent.
2
Extract the shared condition
In both cases, inheritance depends on the owner's confirmation during the sick person's lifetime. If confirmation occurs after death, the acknowledgment is void.
The condition is timing of confirmation.
3
Understand the reasoning
The commentary explains that acknowledgments during illness are analogous to bequests. Like a will, they require acceptance before the testator's death to be binding.
This is a qiyas (analogy) to the rules of wasiyyah.
4
Note the authority
The rulings come from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad via Hasan ibn Ziyad. This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school for this issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال محمد مريض أقر لعبد رجل أنه ابنه ثم مات قال أبو يوسف: إن صدقه السيد في حياة المريض ورثه لأنه ثبت نسبه منه بتصادقهما، فإن صدقه بعد موته لا يرثه لأن إقراره قد بطل بموته. وذكر الحسن بن زياد عن أبي يوسف في مريض له ابن معروف وهو عبد لرجل فأقر المريض أن المولى قد أعتق ابنه قال إن صدقه في حياته ورثه إذا مات، وإن صدقه بعد موته لم يرثه لما بينا
Muhammad said: A sick person acknowledged that the slave of a man is his son, then died. Abu Yusuf said: If the owner confirms during the sick person's lifetime, the slave inherits from him because his lineage is established by their mutual confirmation. If he confirms after his death, he does not inherit because his acknowledgment became void upon his death. Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad reported from Abu Yusuf regarding a sick person who had a known son who was a slave of a man, and the sick person acknowledged that the master had freed his son. He said: If he confirms during his lifetime, the son inherits from him when he dies; if he confirms after his death, he does not inherit, for the reasons stated.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage presents two related cases from Imam Muhammad in Al-Mabsut, reported by Abu Yusuf and through Hasan ibn Ziyad. The first case: a person during his terminal illness states that a certain slave of another man is his son. If the slave's owner confirms this during the sick person's lifetime, the slave inherits from the declarant because lineage is established through mutual acknowledgment (taṣāduq). If the owner confirms only after the declarant's death, the acknowledgment is void because the declarant's right to claim lineage ends at death. The second case: a sick man has a known son who is enslaved by another. The sick man says that the owner has freed his son. If the owner confirms this during the sick man's lifetime, the son inherits (since he becomes free and lineage is recognized). If confirmation comes after death, inheritance is denied. The underlying principle is that acknowledgments made during illness are treated like bequests; they are effective only if conditions are met before the declarant's death.

Key Terms
الإقرار (al-iqrār): A statement by a person that another has a right against him; here, acknowledgment of paternity or freeing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf, in the case of a sick person acknowledging a slave as his son, when does the slave inherit?
A) If the owner confirms at any time before the slave's death
B) If the owner confirms during the sick person's lifetime
C) If the sick person confirms it in his will
D) Regardless of when the owner confirms

Key Takeaway
A sick person's acknowledgment of lineage or freeing requires confirmation by the other party during his lifetime to effect inheritance; otherwise, it lapses at death.

The Method of Calculating the Circulating Share in Spousal Gifts During Illness
Explanation of the differing methods of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad for division when spouses exchange gifts during illness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the differing methods of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani for handling the circulating share (sahm da'ir) in spousal gifts during terminal illness and identify which method is preferred in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad agree on the final ruling but differ in method: who controls the denominator for the circulating share?

When spouses exchange gifts during a terminal illness, a unique accounting problem arises: the same property may circulate back through inheritance. Abu Hanifa and his student Muhammad al-Shaybani both arrive at the same final rulings for standard cases, but their methods of calculation differ. This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the foundational principle (aṣl) behind their dispute and settles on Abu Hanifa's view as the correct one. Understanding this methodological difference deepens your appreciation of how Hanafi jurists resolve complex interactions between gifts and inheritance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core agreement
First, note that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad agree on the final rulings for all cases in this chapter. The dispute is purely about the method (takhārīj) of calculating the division.
2
State Abu Hanifa's method
Abu Hanifa considers the testator's entire property (jamīʿ al-māl) in the division and subtracts the circulating share from the total estate. His reasoning: the circular share arises from property acquired through inheritance, and if no inheritance occurred (e.g., due to debt), there would be no circulation.
3
State Muhammad's method
Muhammad considers only the property actually bequeathed (al-māl al-mūṣā bihī) and subtracts the circulating share from the inheritance acquired via the bequest. He argues that circulation occurs from the bequest itself; if nothing were inherited from the bequest, there would be no circulation.
4
Analyze the evidence for each view
The author explains that the bequest to the wife and her bequest back to the husband are ultimately distributed from the husband's property (māl al-zawj). Therefore, the operation is on his property, making Abu Hanifa's approach more appropriate.
This is a talil (reasoning) based on the source of distribution.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The passage explicitly states 'al-ṣaḥīḥ mā qālahu Abū Ḥanīfa' (the correct view is what Abu Hanifa said). Abu Hanifa's method is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.
Tarjih authority: The author of Bahr al-Ra'iq (likely following Al-Hidayah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو وهب أحد الزوجين لصاحبه في المرض أصله أن أجوبتهم لمسائل الباب متفقة وتخاريجهم لها مختلفة فأبو حنيفة اعتبر جميع الموصي في القسمة وطرح السهم الدائر من جملة المال لأن الدور يقع بسبب المال المستفاد بالميراث وأنه لو لم يرث منها شيئاً بأن كان عليها دين مستغرق لجميع ماله لم يقع الدور، ومحمد اعتبر القسمة في المال الموصى به وطرح السهم الدائر من المال المستفاد بالوصية لأن الدور يقع من ذلك فإنه لو لم يستفد شيئاً بالوصية بأن كان على الزوج دين مستغرق يقع الدور، والصحيح ما قاله أبو حنيفة لأن الوصية للمرأة والمرأة للزوج من وصيتها إنما توزع من مال الزوج لا من مالها فكان العمل من ماله فكان طرح السهم الدائر من نصيبه أولى
If one of the spouses gifts to the other during illness, the origin is that their answers to the issues of the chapter are in agreement, but their derivations differ. Abu Hanifa considered the entire property of the testator in the division and subtracted the circulating share from the total property because the circulation occurs due to property acquired through inheritance, and if he had not inherited anything from her—such as if she had a debt that consumed all her property—then circulation would not occur. Muhammad considered the division in the property that was bequeathed and subtracted the circulating share from the property acquired through the bequest because circulation occurs from that; for if he had not acquired anything through the bequest—such as if the husband had a debt that consumed all—then circulation would occur. The correct view is what Abu Hanifa said because the bequest to the woman and the woman's bequest to the husband are distributed only from the husband's property, not from her property, so the operation is on his property, and thus subtracting the circulating share from his portion is more appropriate.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage establishes the general principle (aṣl) for gifts (hiba) between spouses during terminal illness. The three scholars (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree on the final ruling for each case, but their methods (takhārīj) of calculation differ. Abu Hanifa takes the total estate of the husband (including what he might inherit from his wife) and subtracts any 'circulating share' (sahm dā'ir) from the whole. The circulating share is the portion that returns to the husband through inheritance from his wife, creating a circular calculation. Abu Hanifa argues that since the bequest comes from the husband's property, the circularity should be resolved from his share. Muhammad considers only the property actually bequeathed, subtracting the circular share from the inheritance received via the bequest. The author declares Abu Hanifa's view as correct (al-ṣaḥīḥ), because ultimately the bequests flow from the husband's wealth. This is a key methodological difference in Hanafi law for complex inheritance-gift interactions.

Key Terms
السهم الدائر (al-sahm al-dā'ir): The share that circulates between two parties due to inheritance; e.g., the portion a husband inherits from his wife that he had given as a gift.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which imam's method for handling the 'circulating share' is considered correct?
A) Abu Yusuf
B) Muhammad al-Shaybani
C) Abu Hanifa
D) Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad

Key Takeaway
In intra-Hanafi disputes over method, the mufta bihi position often follows Abu Hanifa when the final rulings agree but derivations differ.

Faraid: Husband Gifts to Wife in Terminal Illness, She Predeceases
Faraid case with overlapping gift and bequest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance shares when a terminally ill husband gifts his only property to his wife who predeceases him, applying the Hanafi principle that the gift remains valid as both a real gift and a bequest.

Core Idea
A gift in terminal illness is both a gift and a bequest; it does not lapse if the donee dies first.

This lesson examines a unique faraid scenario where a husband during his terminal illness gives his entire estate to his wife. The wife then dies before the husband, and later the husband also dies. The key legal issue: does the gift lapse because the wife died first? The Hanafi answer is no, because the gift is a real gift (hiba haqiqiyya) completed by possession, though it is also treated as a bequest (wasiyya) for the one-third rule. The final distribution yields 80% to the husband's heirs and 20% to the wife's agnates. We will walk through the reasoning and the three takhrij methods of the Hanafi imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the parties
Recognize that the husband has only 100 dirhams, gifts it to his wife during terminal illness, she dies first, then he dies. Heirs: husband's agnates (asaba) and wife's agnates (asaba). No children are mentioned, so husband inherits half of wife's estate if he survived her.
The wife becomes a non-heir (ajnabiyya) when she dies before the husband.
2
Understand the dual nature of the gift
The gift is a real gift (hiba haqiqiyya) because possession was taken, so it does not lapse upon the donee's death. But because it is from a terminally ill person, it is also a bequest (wasiyya hukman) and subject to the one-third limit from the estate. So the wife's share is both: she owns the 100 immediately, but for inheritance purposes, only one-third is effective as a bequest from the husband's estate. The rest is treated as a gift from the husband.
This dual treatment prevents the gift from lapsing.
3
Follow Abu Hanifa's derivation (takhrij)
Abu Hanifa starts with the 100 as the husband's estate. He divides it into three shares: one share for the wife's bequest (which is one-third of the 100, i.e., 33.33) and two shares for the husband (66.66). The wife dies leaving her share; it is divided equally between husband and her agnates (since no children). The husband inherits half of her share, creating a 'circulating share' that is subtracted from his portion. After adjustments, the husband's total becomes 80, wife's agnates get 20.
The base number becomes 5 after correction.
4
Compare with Abu Yusuf's and Muhammad's derivations
Abu Yusuf considers the husband's property as what he inherits from his wife (16.66 dirhams) plus the gift adjustment, leading to the same final 80/20. Muhammad uses the wife's one-third (33.33) as the base, divides into shares, and arrives at the same result. All three methods confirm the outcome.
The differences are in starting assumptions, but the final numbers are agreed upon.
5
Verify the final distribution
After all calculations: husband's heirs receive 80 dirhams (80%), wife's agnates receive 20 dirhams (20%). The wife's bequest (40) is half of the husband's estate, but because the husband inherits back half of her share, the net effect is the 80/20 split.
This distribution is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم المسائل على فصول: أحدها في هبة الزوج لامرأته في مرضه، والثاني في هبته في مرضه لامرأته ووصيته لأجنبي، والثالث في هبة كل واحد من الزوجين لصاحبه. وإذا وهب لامرأته في مرضه مائة لا مال له غيرها وماتت ومات وتركت عصبة للزوج لورثة درهم الزوج ستون ببعض الهبة وجازت في أربعين للزوج من ذلك عشرة بميراثه ولعصبتها عشرون لأنها لما ماتت قبل موت الزوج صارت أجنبية ولم تبق وارثة قبل موت الزوج فصحت الهبة لها فلم تبطل الهبة لها، وإن كانت الهبة المنفذة وصية والوصية تبطل موت الموصى له قبل موت الموصي لأنها هبة حقيقية حتى ملكها الموهوب له في الحال وصية حكماً حتى الثلث والهبة لا تبطل بموت الموهوب له قبل موت الواهب بعد ما تمت بالقبض، وباعتبار وصية تنفذ من الثلث عملاً بالشبهين ولا يجوز إبطالها بالشك بعد صحتها. ثم تخريجه أن لأبي حنيفة وهو المائة الموهوبة فيجعل على ثلاثة أسهم لحاجتين لأجل المال للزوج جميع الوصية للمرأة وذلك سهم وسهمان للزوج ماتت المرأة عن سهم فيكون ميراث ميراثاً وعصبتها نصفين وقد انكسر بالنصف فأضعف فصار ستة فصار للزوج أربعة ولها سهمان فيعود إلى الزوج سهم بالميراث منها وهو السهم الدائر فاطرحه من نصيب الزوج فكان نصيبه أربعة فبقي له ثلاث ولها سهمان فصار جميع مال الزوج على خمسة خمسا المائة وذلك أربعون لها بالوصية وللزوج ثلاثة أخماسها ستون، ثم يعود إلى الزوج نصف حصتها بالميراث فصار للزوج ثمانون ولعصبتها عشرون وأما تخريج أبي يوسف وهو أن مال الزوج ما يرث منها لا جميع ما وهب منها لأن هذه هبة منفذة ولهذا لا تبطل بموتها قبل موت الزوج فيعتبر بما لو وهبها في الصحة ثم ماتت والزوج وارثتها يعتبر مال الزوج ما ورث منها لا جميع الموهوب فكذا هذا، وقد ورث الزوج منها ستة عشر درهماً وثلثي درهم لأن لها ثلث المائة ثلاثة وثلاثين وثلث فيكون للزوج نصفه وذلك ستة عشر درهماً وثلثان، ثم لها خمسا ستة عشر بعد طرح السهم الدائر من الوجه الذي بينا وذلك ستة دراهم وثلثان يضم إلى ما أعطينا لها في الابتداء وذلك ثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث فصار لها أربعون ثم يرث الزوج منها عشرين فيصير لورثة الزوج ثمانون. وأما تخريج محمد بأن لها ثلث المائة وذلك ثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث فيجعل ذلك المال على سهمين لحاجتك إلى النصف للزوج بالميراث فيكون لها ثلث ذلك السهم بالوصية فانكسر بالثلث فاضرب أصل الفريضة وذلك سهمان في ثلاثة فصار ستة فاطرح السهم الدائر من جميع السهام فصار خمسة فلها خمسي ثلاثة وثلاثين وثلث وذلك ستة دراهم وثلثان فصار لها أربعون وللورثة ثمانون
Then the issues are divided into sections: the first is the gift of a husband to his wife during his illness; the second is his gift to his wife and bequest to a stranger; the third is the gift of each spouse to the other. If a husband gifts to his wife during his illness one hundred dirhams, having no other property, and she dies and he dies, leaving agnates for the husband, the heirs get: the husband sixty by some of the gift, and it is valid for forty; for the husband ten from that by inheritance, and for her agnates twenty. Because when she died before the husband's death, she became a stranger (non-heir) and did not remain an heir before the husband's death, so the gift was valid for her; thus the gift does not become invalid for her. Although the executed gift is a bequest, and a bequest becomes invalid by the death of the legatee before the testator, it is a real gift such that the donee owns it immediately, and a bequest in terms of the one-third rule; a gift does not become invalid by the death of the donee before the death of the donor after it is completed by possession. And considering it a bequest executed from the one-third by acting on both aspects, it is not permissible to invalidate it by doubt after its validity. Then its derivation according to Abu Hanifa: he considers the gifted one hundred; he divides it into three shares for two needs: for the estate of the husband, the entire bequest to the woman is one share, and two shares for the husband. The woman dies leaving one share, so one share becomes inheritance between her husband and her agnates. It is divided into halves, and it breaks by half, so he doubles, making six. So the husband gets four, she gets two. Then one share returns to the husband from her by inheritance, which is the circulating share; he subtracts it from the husband's portion. So his portion was four; three remains for him, and two for her. So the entire property of the husband becomes five-fifths: two-fifths of the hundred, which is forty, for her by bequest, and three-fifths, sixty, for the husband. Then half of her share returns to the husband by inheritance, so the husband gets eighty, and her agnates twenty. As for the derivation of Abu Yusuf: he considers the husband's property as what he inherits from her, not all that he gave, because this is an executed gift, and thus it does not become invalid by her death before the husband. He analogizes to if he had given her in health and then she died and the husband is her heir: the husband's property is what he inherits from her, not all that he gave. So here similarly. He inherited from her sixteen and two-thirds dirhams because she has one-third of the hundred (thirty-three and one-third); half of that is sixteen and two-thirds. Then she has two-fifths of sixteen after subtracting the circulating share in the manner we explained, which is six and two-thirds, added to what we gave her initially (thirty-three and one-third), making forty. Then the husband inherits twenty from her, so the husband's heirs get eighty. As for the derivation of Muhammad: she has one-third of the hundred (thirty-three and one-third). He divides that property into two shares because of the need for half for the husband by inheritance; so she has one-third of that share by bequest. It breaks by one-third; multiply the base of the estate (two shares) by three, making six. Subtract the circulating share from all the shares, leaving five. So she gets two-fifths of thirty-three and one-third, which is six and two-thirds; so she gets forty, and the heirs get eighty.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This is the first specific case (fard) under the chapter: a husband during his terminal illness gifts his entire property (100 dirhams) to his wife, then the wife dies before the husband, then the husband dies leaving agnates. The passage first gives the final distribution: husband's heirs get 80, wife's agnates get 20. The reason is that the gift is a real gift (hiba ḥaqīqiyya) that is executed immediately by possession, so it does not lapse if the donee dies before the donor. However, because it is from a terminally ill person, it is also treated as a bequest (waṣiyya) subject to the one-third rule. Acting on both aspects, the gift is valid for the entire amount but only one-third is effective from the estate; the rest is treated as a gift. Then the passage provides three methods (takhārīj) by Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad for arriving at the same final numbers. Abu Hanifa's method: treat the 100 as the estate. Divide it into three shares: two for the husband (since he will inherit half of his wife's share) and one for the wife. After her death, her share is divided between husband and her agnates. The circular share (the portion the husband inherits from her) is subtracted from his portion. Final: husband's heirs get 80, wife's 20. Abu Yusuf takes a different starting point: the husband's property is only what he inherits from his wife (since the gift is executed). He calculates her share as one-third of 100, then half of that (16.66), then adds the gift adjustment to reach 40 for wife, 80 for husband. Muhammad's method: use her one-third as base, divide into shares, subtract circular share, leading to same result. The point is that although methods differ, the final answer is agreed upon.

Key Terms
تخريج (takhrij): A method of deriving the ruling from principles; here, each imam's way of reaching the same division.
هبة حقيقية (hiba haqiqiyya): Real gift, completed by possession, not dependent on the donor's death.
وصية حكماً (wasiyya hukman): Constructive bequest; treated as a bequest for legal purposes (e.g., one-third limit) though it is a real gift.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first case of husband gifting to wife in terminal illness, what is the final amount that goes to the wife's agnates?
A) 40
B) 20
C) 60
D) 80

Key Takeaway
A gift made during terminal illness does not lapse if the donee predeceases the donor, and the distribution involves treating the gift as both a real gift and a bequest, resulting in an 80/20 split between the donor's heirs and the donee's agnates.

Gift to Wife in Illness: Validity and Calculation
Calculation of the wife's bequest and inheritance when she predeceases the husband

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the distribution of a gift made in terminal illness when the donee predeceases the donor, using both Abu Hanifa's and Muhammad's methods, and state the principle that the gift is valid by analogy to a gift in health.

Core Idea
A gift in terminal illness is valid; the wife's predecease does not void it, but proper calculation requires eliminating the revolving share.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hanafi law: a husband gifts his entire estate to his wife during his terminal illness, and she dies before him. The gift is not invalidated, but the wife's estate becomes subject to inheritance by the husband. Calculating the final shares requires careful handling of a 'revolving share' (السهم الدائر) to avoid double counting. We will study the legal principle and walk through two calculation methods that yield the same result.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario and legal principle
Identify the scenario: a husband gives a gift to his wife during terminal illness; she predeceases him. The gift is valid (sahih) because it is an executed gift, analogous to a gift in health. Note that the wife is an heir, so the gift is also treated as a bequest (wasiyya) limited to 1/3 of the estate when there are other heirs.
The passage assumes the husband's total estate is 100 dirhams and that other heirs exist besides the wife.
2
Apply the analogy (qiyas)
The ruling is based on qiyas jaliy: a gift in illness is like a gift in health. The effective cause (illa) is that the gift is executed (munfadha). Therefore, the gift does not become void upon the wife's death.
The dalil from the text: 'فيعتبر بما لو وهبها في الصحة' – 'So it is considered like if he gifted it in health.'
3
Identify the revolving share (al-sahm al-dā'ir)
The wife initially receives 1/3 of the estate as bequest (33.333 dirhams). When she dies, the husband inherits half of her estate (16.667 dirhams). This inherited amount is part of the original gift that returns to the husband, creating a 'revolving share' that must be eliminated to avoid double counting.
The revolving share is the amount that is counted both as part of the wife's bequest and as part of the husband's inheritance.
4
Follow Abu Hanifa's calculation method
Step 1: Wife's initial bequest = 1/3 of 100 = 33.333. Step 2: Husband inherits half of that = 16.667. Step 3: Subtract the revolving share from the 16.667 (the method of subtraction is detailed in the text). Step 4: Wife gets 2/5 of the remainder (after subtraction) = 6.667. Step 5: Add this to the initial bequest: 33.333 + 6.667 = 40. Step 6: Husband then inherits 20 from the wife's final estate (half of 40), so husband's heirs total: 100 - 40 + 20? Actually careful: The husband's heirs ultimately receive 80 dirhams (the original 100 minus the wife's 40 plus the inheritance from wife? The text says: 'ثم يرث الزوج منها عشرين فيصير لورثة الزوج ثمانون' – then the husband inherits twenty from her, so the husband's heirs get eighty. This means the husband's heirs receive the original 100 minus the wife's 40 (60) plus the inheritance from wife? Actually calculation: Wife's estate is 40, husband inherits 20 from that, so husband's total wealth becomes 100 - 40 (the gift) + 20 = 80? Or simply the original 100 is redistributed: wife retains 40, husband's heirs get 80 (since the husband's inheritance of 20 from wife is already included in the 80). The final result is: wife's estate = 40, husband's heirs = 80.
The numbers work out: 33.333 + 6.667 = 40; half of 40 = 20; 100 - 40 = 60; 60 + 20 = 80. But the text directly says the heirs get 80.
5
Follow Muhammad's calculation method
Muhammad's method yields the same result using a different fractional approach. He takes the wife's bequest of 33.333, divides it into 2 shares (because husband gets half by inheritance), then determines that the wife gets 1/3 of one share as bequest. After clearing denominators (multiplying by 3), he subtracts the revolving share, leaving 5 shares out of 6. Thus the wife gets 2/5 of the original bequest (6.667) added to the initial 33.333, culminating in 40. The heirs get 80.
Both methods agree on the final distribution: wife 40, heirs 80.

Source Text

جميع ما وهب منها لأن هذه هبة منفذة ولهذا لا تبطل بموتها قبل موت الزوج فيعتبر بما لو وهبها في الصحة ثم ماتت والزوج وارثتها يعتبر مال الزوج ما ورث منها لا جميع الموهوب فكذا هذا، وقد ورث الزوج منها ستة عشر درهماً وثلثي درهم لأن لها ثلث المائة ثلاثة وثلاثين وثلث فيكون للزوج نصفه وذلك ستة عشر درهماً وثلثان، ثم لها خمسا ستة عشر بعد طرح السهم الدائر من الوجه الذي بينا وذلك ستة دراهم وثلثان يضم إلى ما أعطينا لها في الابتداء وذلك ثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث فصار لها أربعون ثم يرث الزوج منها عشرين فيصير لورثة الزوج ثمانون. وأما تخريج محمد بأن لها ثلث المائة وذلك ثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث فيجعل ذلك المال على سهمين لحاجتك إلى النصف للزوج بالميراث فيكون لها ثلث ذلك السهم بالوصية فانكسر بالثلث فاضرب أصل الفريضة وذلك سهمان في ثلاثة فصار ستة فاطرح السهم الدائر من جميع السهام فصار خمسة فلها خمسي ثلاثة وثلاثين وثلث وذلك ستة دراهم وثلثان فصار لها أربعون وللورثة ثمانون
All of what was gifted from it, because this is an executed gift, and therefore it is not invalidated by her death before the death of the husband. So it is considered like if he gifted it in health, then she died and the husband is her heir. The husband's wealth is considered what he inherited from her, not all of the gifted property. Similarly here. And the husband inherited from her sixteen and two-thirds dirhams, because she has one-third of one hundred: thirty-three and one-third, so the husband gets half of that, which is sixteen and two-thirds. Then she has two-fifths of sixteen after subtracting the revolving share in the manner we explained, which is six and two-thirds, added to what we gave her initially, which is thirty-three and one-third, so she gets forty. Then the husband inherits twenty from her, so the husband's heirs get eighty. As for the derivation of Muhammad, that she has one-third of one hundred, which is thirty-three and one-third. He makes that wealth into two shares because you need half for the husband by inheritance, so she has one-third of that share by bequest. It is broken by one-third, so multiply the original division, which is two shares, by three, making six. Subtract the revolving share from all the shares, leaving five. So she has two-fifths of thirty-three and one-third, which is six and two-thirds dirhams, so she gets forty, and the heirs get eighty.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on a gift made by a husband to his wife during his terminal illness, where the wife predeceases the husband. The text establishes that the gift is valid and not invalidated by the wife's prior death, analogizing it to a gift made in health. The calculation of the wife's bequest and inheritance involves two methods: one attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa and another to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. Both methods yield the same final distribution: the wife effectively receives 40 dirhams (considering the gift and inheritance), and the husband's heirs receive 80 dirhams from the original 100. The key concept is the 'revolving share' (السهم الدائر), which is the share that returns to the husband by inheritance and is eliminated from the calculation to avoid double counting.

Key Terms
السهم الدائر (al-sahm al-dā'ir): The share that is counted in the initial bequest but then returns to the husband by inheritance, which must be eliminated to avoid duplication.
هبة منفذة (hiba munfadha): An executed gift – a gift that has been delivered and taken effect.
قياس جلي (qiyas jaliy): An evident analogy – one in which the effective cause (illa) is clear and unambiguous.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 33.33 dirhams
B) 40 dirhams
C) 60 dirhams
D) 80 dirhams

Key Takeaway
A gift in terminal illness is valid; the final distribution (wife 40%, heirs 60%) is achieved by eliminating the revolving share through careful calculation.

Bequest Calculation with Wife's Additional Property
Calculation of bequest with wife's own property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the valid bequest amount when the wife possesses additional property of her own, applying the Hanafi rule of one-third and two-thirds.

Core Idea
The wife's additional property changes the husband's estate size, but the bequest still holds to one-third.

In this passage, we examine a scenario where a wife who received a bequest also has her own additional wealth. This affects the total estate and the calculation of the valid bequest. We will walk through the arithmetic step by step to see how the one-third/two-thirds ratio is preserved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the variables
The husband's initial wealth is 250 dirhams (the gifted 100 plus the inherited 50 from the wife). The wife has an additional 100 dirhams of her own.
The 'revolving share' refers to the part that returns to the husband via inheritance.
2
Calculate the wife's bequest
The wife's bequest is two-fifths of the husband's wealth after subtracting the revolving share. Two-fifths of 250 = 100 dirhams.
Two-fifths is the fraction from the previous case.
3
Determine the return by inheritance
Half of the bequest (50 dirhams) returns to the husband by inheritance, so the husband ends with 200 dirhams.
The husband inherits half of the wife's estate (including the bequest).
4
Verify the ratio
The bequest executed (100 dirhams) is one-third of the husband's final estate (300 dirhams total? Actually the estate is the husband's 200 plus the wife's remaining? The text says 'third and two-thirds are established' meaning the bequest is one-third of the total estate after adjustments.)
The 'third and two-thirds' refers to the bequest being one-third and the residue two-thirds.

ولو كان لها مائة أخرى والمسألة بحالها فإنه يرد إلى ورثة الزوج عشرون درهماً ببطلان الهبة وأربعون درهماً بالميراث وتخريجه أن مال الزوج مائتا درهم وخمسون درهماً وللمرأة بالوصية خمسا ذلك بعد طرح السهم الدائر وذلك مائة ثم يعود إلى الزوج نصفها بالميراث وذلك خمسون فصار للزوج مائتان وقد نفذنا الوصية في مائة فاستقام الثلث والثلثان
And if she had another hundred dirhams and the case is the same, then twenty dirhams are returned to the husband's heirs due to the invalidation of the gift, and forty dirhams by inheritance. Its derivation: the husband's wealth is two hundred and fifty dirhams, and the woman by bequest has two-fifths of that after subtracting the revolving share, which is one hundred. Then half of it returns to the husband by inheritance, which is fifty, so the husband gets two hundred. We have executed the bequest in one hundred, so the third and two-thirds are established.

Commentary
This case adds that the wife has an additional 100 dirhams of her own property. The calculation now involves the husband's total wealth (the gifted 100 plus the inherited 50 from the wife's estate, totaling 250). The wife's bequest is two-fifths of that after deducting the revolving share, resulting in 100. Half of that (50) returns to the husband by inheritance, leaving him with 200 total. The gift is thus valid in 100 dirhams, maintaining the one-third/two-thirds ratio.

Key Terms
الثلث والثلثان (al-thuluth wa al-thuluthān): The one-third and two-thirds ratio that must hold in bequests from the estate.

Validity of a Gift When Husband's Only Asset is the Gifted Amount
Calculation of gift validity with inheritance adjustment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the valid portion of a gift (hiba) when the donor's only asset is the gifted property, applying the one-third bequest limit and inheritance adjustment.

Core Idea
A gift from a husband to a wife may be only partially valid if it exceeds one-third of his total estate.

This passage presents a specific calculation problem in Hanafi inheritance and bequest law. The husband gifts 100 dirhams to his wife, who already has 200 dirhams of her own. At his death, his only asset is that same 100 dirhams. The gift must be tested against the one-third bequest limit, and the wife's inheritance share must be factored in. The result is a partial validity of 60 dirhams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the assets
Determine what the husband owns at the time of division: the gifted 100 dirhams plus an inheritance from the wife (because she dies first, leaving him a share of her 200). Wife's 200 is divided: husband gets 50 (1/4 as spouse) and the rest goes to her asaba. So husband's total estate becomes 150.
The wife's death creates an inheritance that increases the husband's assets.
2
Apply the one-third rule for bequests
A bequest (including a gift made in contemplation of death) is limited to one-third of the estate. The husband's estate is 150, so the maximum bequest is 50. However, the gift is 100, so it exceeds the limit. Only 50 would normally be valid, but the calculation yields 60 due to the revolving share adjustment.
The 'revolving share' (al-sahm al-da'ir) adjusts the fractions.
3
Compute the shares after inheritance
Initially, the estate (150) is divided into 3 shares: wife gets 1 (50), husband gets 2 (100). But the wife's share (50) reverts as inheritance: husband takes half as spouse (25), and the other half goes to her asaba. This creates a complex fractional distribution.
The wife's share becomes divided between husband and asaba.
4
Resolve the fraction with doubling
To avoid fractions, double the number of shares: wife now gets 2 shares (instead of 1), husband gets 4 (instead of 2). After inheritance, one share returns to husband, so he ends with 5 shares total. The 'revolving' share is the one that cycles back; subtract it from his share.
Doubling produces whole numbers.
5
Determine the valid gift amount
The husband's estate is now represented by 5 shares. The wife's right (from the gift) is 2 shares, which is 2/5 of 150 = 60. So the gift is valid for 60 dirhams, not 100. The remaining 40 returns to the husband, then half of the wife's 60 (i.e., 30) returns to him via inheritance, leaving him with 120.
Final distribution: husband 120, wife's estate 60 (gift valid for 60).

The husband's estate is adjusted to 150 (100 gift + 50 inheritance from wife), and through fractional adjustments, the wife receives 60 by bequest, with 40 returned to the husband. The final distribution sees the husband with 120 and the wife's estate effectively receiving 60, maintaining the one-third/two-thirds ratio.

Key Terms
العصبة (al-ʿaṣabah): The agnatic heirs who inherit the residue after fixed shares.
السهم الدائر (al-sahm al-dā'ir): The share that revolves back to the donor through inheritance, subtracted to avoid double counting.

Bequest with Debt: Calculating the Free Portion
Calculation when the husband has a debt of 50 dirhams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the valid bequest amount when the testator has debt, applying the Hanafi rule that debts are settled before bequests and the bequest is limited to one-third of the free estate.

Core Idea
Debts remove their equivalent from the estate; bequests are executed only from the remaining free portion.

This lesson walks through a classic Hanafi example: a husband gifts his wife 100 dirhams in his illness, but he owes 50 dirhams. The wife dies before him. How much does she actually receive? The answer depends on prioritizing debt and the 'revolving share' calculation. Understanding this case is essential for estate planning and wasiyyah rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the estate and debt
The husband's total estate is 100 dirhams (the gifted amount is his entire wealth). He owes 50 dirhams debt. The debt must be satisfied first, leaving 50 dirhams free of debt.
Debt takes priority over bequests by Quranic injunction (4:11-12).
2
Determine the free wealth
The free wealth is the estate minus debt: 100 - 50 = 50 dirhams. This is the amount from which bequests can be made.
The term 'al-māl al-fārigh ʿan al-dayn' is key.
3
Apply the bequest limit of one-third
Bequests are limited to one-third of the free wealth. One-third of 50 is approximately 16.67, but the text arrives at 20 due to a 'revolving share' adjustment (the bequest itself returns part to the testator's estate).
The one-third rule is based on the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas.
4
Calculate the valid bequest with revolving share
The wife was bequeathed 100, but only 50 free. The calculation: she gets two-fifths of 50 (20) by bequest, and the remaining 30 returns to the husband's heirs. Then half of what she got (10) returns to the husband by inheritance, so her heirs get 10, the husband's heirs get 40.
This adjustment ensures the bequest does not exceed one-third of the free estate after considering the return.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو كان على أحدهما دين قضى دينه أو لا ثم ما فضل ينفذ التبرع في ثلثه وهب لامرأته في مرضه مئة لا مال له غيرها وعليه دين خمسون ثم ماتت المرأة قبله أخذ رب الدين خمسين وجازت وصيتها في عشرين يعود نصفه إلى الزوج بالميراث فيكون لورثة الزوج أربعون ولورثتها عشرة لأن الوصية تنفذ من المال الفارغ عن الدين وخمسون درهماً من مال الزوج مشغول بالدين فيجعل كالهالك ويعتبر ماله الفارغ وخمسون وقد أوصى بذلك كله فتنفذ الوصية من الثلث ولها خمسا خمسين بعد طرح السهم الدائر على ما بينا وذلك عشرون فلها عشرون بالوصية وترد ثلاثون على ورثة الزوج ثم يعود نصف ما صار لها بالوصية من الزوج وبالميراث وذلك عشر فصار له أربعون وقد نفذنا الوصية في عشرين
And if one of them had a debt, his debt is paid or not, then whatever remains, the donation is executed from one-third of it. He gifted his wife in his illness one hundred dirhams, he has no wealth besides it, and he owes a debt of fifty. Then the woman died before him. The creditor takes fifty, and her bequest is valid for twenty. Half of it returns to the husband by inheritance, so the husband's heirs get forty and her heirs get ten. Because the bequest is executed from the wealth free of debt, and fifty dirhams of the husband's wealth are occupied by debt, so it is considered like destroyed, and his free wealth is fifty. He bequeathed all of that, so the bequest is executed from one-third. She has two-fifths of fifty after subtracting the revolving share as we explained, which is twenty. So she gets twenty by bequest, and thirty are returned to the husband's heirs. Then half of what she got by bequest returns to the husband by inheritance, which is ten, so he gets forty. We executed the bequest for twenty.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This case introduces debt. The husband owes 50 dirhams, so his net estate is 50 (since the gifted 100 is encumbered by debt). The wife's bequest is calculated from the free portion (50). After eliminating the revolving share, she is entitled to 20 dirhams. Half of that (10) returns to the husband by inheritance, so the husband's heirs receive 40 from the original 100, and the wife's heirs receive 10. The debt is paid first, then the bequest from the remainder.

Key Terms
المال الفارغ عن الدين (al-māl al-fārigh ʿan al-dayn): The portion of the estate that is not encumbered by debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One hundred dirhams
B) Fifty dirhams
C) Twenty dirhams
D) Ten dirhams

Key Takeaway
A bequest is only valid from the estate free of debt; debt must be paid first and the bequest limited to one-third of that free portion.

Gift of Eighty Dirhams with Wife's Debt
A juristic derivation of bequest amount using qiyas and fractional adjustments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the bequest amount when a wife has a debt and the husband is the heir, applying the Hanafi principle of half-debt attribution.

Core Idea
Half of the wife's debt is attributed to the husband because the bequest returns to him by inheritance — the revolving share principle.

This passage presents a nuanced fiqh calculation where a wife receives a gift of 80 dirhams during her marriage, but she also has a debt of 10 dirhams. The husband, being the heir, inherits from her. The key twist: the bequest (gift) is treated as if it returns to the husband, so half of her debt is effectively his. This affects the final shares. Let's walk through the derivation step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial values
The husband gifted his wife 80 dirhams. She also has a debt of 10 dirhams. The husband inherits from her estate.
The gift is a bequest (wasiyyah) that will ultimately return to the husband as an heir.
2
Apply the half-debt attribution principle
Because the bequest will return to the husband by inheritance, half of the wife's debt (5 dirhams) is considered the husband's responsibility in this calculation. So the husband's effective contribution is reduced.
The principle: 'دين المرأة نصفه على الزوج' (half of the woman's debt is upon the husband) in this context.
3
Calculate the husband's net wealth
The husband's wealth is initially 80 (the gift) but because the wife's debt of 10 dirhams is considered 'like destroyed' for the bequest, the husband's effective wealth for calculation becomes 75 dirhams (80 minus half of the debt? Actually it's 80 - 5 = 75, but the text says 'خمسة الزوج وسبعون' which is an OCR error for 'خمسة وسبعون' = 75).
The debt encumbrance is treated as destroying part of the estate.
4
Apply the revolving share adjustment
The husband's 75 dirhams is divided into shares considering that half of the wife's share returns to him. Through a series of fractional adjustments (doubling, subtracting the revolving share), the final bequest amount is determined as 30 dirhams for the wife. From that, the 10 dirham debt is paid, leaving 20; then half (10) returns to the husband, so the wife's heirs effectively get 20? But the text says she gets 60, which seems inconsistent; likely the 60 is after including the returned half? We follow the given ruling: the bequest is 30, debt paid 10, net 20, then half returns to husband (10), leaving 20 for wife's heirs? The text says 'فصار لها ستون' (so she has 60) – this likely means the total estate after adjustments is 60? This passage is complex and may contain OCR errors; the core lesson is the method.
The revolving share (السهم الدائر) is subtracted from the husband's portion.
5
State the final bequest amount
According to the text, the wife's bequest (the amount subject to the will) is 30 dirhams. This is the amount from which her debt is paid and the remainder is distributed.
The derivation shows the juristic method, not a simple arithmetic.
